## 68. Felix Pago

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.felixpago.com) | [Series A coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2024/05/28/felix-pago-raises-15-5-million-to-help-latino-workers-send-money-home-via-whatsapp/) | [QED investment rationale](https://www.qedinvestors.com/blog/why-we-invested-in-felix-pago)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Manuel Godoy | Co-founder and CEO | Identified as CEO in TechCrunch's Series A coverage. |
| Bernardo García | Co-founder | Identified alongside Godoy in the same coverage; TechCrunch notes a third co-founder exists but was not individually named in the article. |

### Product description

Félix Pago is a WhatsApp-native remittance product: users complete a money transfer entirely inside a WhatsApp chat, including by voice message, without downloading a separate app. The platform now supports payouts to ten Latin American countries (Mexico, Guatemala, Honduras, El Salvador, Dominican Republic, Colombia, Nicaragua, Ecuador, Peru, and Costa Rica per the company's current site, up from three countries at the time of the 2024 Series A), with payout via bank deposit, mobile wallet, or cash pickup at more than 40,000 partner locations. Behind the scenes, Félix uses Circle's USDC stablecoin to source and settle foreign exchange, which TechCrunch reported reduces FX costs and pre-funding needs, enabling a free first transfer and a flat $2.50 fee on many subsequent transfers to core corridors.

### Thesis: why invest

Remittances from the U.S. to Latin America are a large, recurring, and still meaningfully priced-inefficient flow, and Félix's WhatsApp-native interface removes the app-download friction that is a real barrier for its target user (blue-collar Latino workers in construction, food service, and home services). The May 2024 $15.5m Series A was led by Castle Island Ventures (a Boston-based crypto-focused fund) with Switch Ventures, HTwenty, MELI Capital (Mercado Libre's venture arm), and Contour returning; Félix has also disclosed partnerships with Mercado Pago and Nubank, both credible distribution signals in the region. Since inception the company has said more than 300,000 users have sent over $1 billion combined through the platform.

The moat is distribution-plus-cost: a referral-driven, chat-native product with stablecoin-powered FX economics is hard for a legacy player (Western Union) to replicate without cannibalizing its own fee structure, and hard for a pure crypto rail to replicate without Félix's retail trust and WhatsApp UX. The risk is that this same moat is replicable by other well-funded LatAm remittance and neobank challengers, and Félix's own growth (previously reported near 30% month-over-month) is not disclosed at a current, comparable rate.

**What must be true:** referral-driven growth must continue without materially rising paid-acquisition cost; the ten-country payout network must maintain reliable partner-location uptime and compliance across jurisdictions with different money-transmission regimes; stablecoin FX arbitrage economics must hold as competitors also adopt similar rails; and Félix must show it can retain users past the free-first-transfer hook.

**Next-round milestones:** $2bn-plus in cumulative processed volume, disclosed current revenue and take-rate figures, expansion into at least two of the additionally listed corridors with proven compliance, and evidence that referral-driven CAC remains materially below paid-acquisition benchmarks for the category.

### Founder bet

Godoy and García (plus an unnamed third co-founder) built a genuinely differentiated distribution mechanic — WhatsApp-native transfer — in a category where most competitors still require a dedicated app. Diligence should confirm the full founding team and assess whether the product's simplicity is defensible or a feature any well-funded competitor could ship within a product cycle.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |

### Public comps and exit model

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($82.8m) at 1.0x floor (0.8x floored) = $82.8m EV, $1.92m proceeds, 0.77x — a capital-loss scenario. Upside detail: 150% of base revenue ($207m) at one turn more (2.8x) = $579.6m EV, $13.45m proceeds, 5.38x.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Stablecoin dependency:** the FX-cost advantage depends on continued USDC liquidity, Circle's operating stability, and favorable regulatory treatment of stablecoin-based remittance rails. Require exposure limits and a contingency plan if stablecoin regulation tightens.
- **Compliance across ten corridors:** each payout country has its own money-transmission and AML regime. Require a full licensing map and evidence of consistent partner-location uptime.
- **Full entry pricing:** at the $70m HCP assumed post-money, base MOIC is a modest 2.31x. Invest because the WhatsApp-native distribution edge and MELI Capital/Nubank partnerships are real, differentiated signals — but seek a lower effective entry price or firmer current revenue disclosure before committing at this level.
- **Growth-rate disclosure gap:** the ~30% MoM figure is from 2024 reporting; confirm current growth rate, since remittance apps often see deceleration as they scale past early-adopter cohorts.

## 69. Metaview

**Stage:** Series B (stage exception — see note below)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.metaview.ai/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.metaview.ai/resources/blog/fresh-capital-announcement) | [Series B announcement](https://www.metaview.ai/resources/blog/series-b) | [GV investment profile](https://www.gv.com/news/metaview-ai-hiring)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Siadhal Magos | Co-founder | Previously at Uber and Palantir; co-founded Metaview in 2018 per company sourcing. |
| Shahriar Tajbakhsh | Co-founder and CTO | Previously at Uber and Palantir; leads technical development of Metaview's interview-intelligence platform. |

### Product description

Metaview is an AI interview-intelligence platform for recruiting teams: an AI notetaker captures interviews, generates structured reports, and feeds a broader hiring workflow that now extends to job-post generation and candidate search. The company has captured and analyzed more than 3 million interviews across its customer base, per its own reporting, and serves customers including Deel, Brex, Deliveroo, and Quora. Its wedge is treating the interview itself — historically a black box of unstructured notes and inconsistent scoring — as a structured data asset that improves hiring-decision quality and consistency.

### Thesis: why invest

**Stage exception:** the roster flagged Metaview as a Series A target; the company has since progressed. It raised a $7m Series A in March 2024 led by Plural, then a $35m (€30m) Series B in June 2025 led by GV (Alphabet's venture arm), with continuing participation from Plural, Vertex Ventures, and Seedcamp, bringing total disclosed funding to approximately $50m. Per this batch's mandate, HCP retains Metaview with this exception explained rather than swapping it out, but prices the return model off current Series B economics rather than the original Series A framing — which materially compresses achievable ownership for a $1.0m-$2.5m check.

The company discloses more than 3,000 customers and 3-plus million interviews captured, alongside claims of 30-plus minutes saved per hiring conversation and a 30% decrease in interviews per hire — company-reported figures. GV's lead on the Series B is a credible signal of institutional conviction in the interview-intelligence category specifically (distinct from broader HR-suite plays).

**What must be true:** the 3,000+ customer base must convert meaningfully into expansion revenue as interview volumes grow with each customer's hiring; Metaview must maintain a data and workflow moat as general-purpose meeting-intelligence tools (Gong, Otter, native Zoom AI) push into adjacent territory; and post-Series B growth must justify the implied valuation step-up for later investors.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed Series B valuation and use-of-proceeds detail, $40m+ ARR, net revenue retention above 125%, and expansion into structured candidate-search and job-post workflows generating meaningful incremental revenue per account.

### Founder bet

Siadhal Magos and Shahriar Tajbakhsh bring a credible technical pairing from Uber and Palantir, and have sustained the company since a 2018 founding through a Series A and now a GV-led Series B — a long, patient build in a category (interview intelligence) that only became broadly investable once large language models made structured transcript analysis practical. The seven-year founding-to-Series-B timeline suggests resilience, though it also means Metaview weathered a long period before the category's current AI-driven tailwind arrived.

The $150m HCP-assumption post-money is a placeholder for an undisclosed Series B valuation; a $2.0m check at this stage buys meaningfully less ownership than the same check would have at the original Series A, which is the central driver of this memo's modest return profile.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price:** the core issue in this memo is not the business but the price — a $2.0m check at Series B economics for a company with an undisclosed but likely $150m+ post-money buys thin ownership. Invest only with a lower effective price (secondary, side-letter terms, or a smaller allocation reserved for a later round where HCP has better information).
- **Category compression:** general-purpose meeting-intelligence tools (Gong, Otter, native video-platform AI) could extend into recruiting and commoditize transcript capture. Metaview's defense is recruiting-specific structured workflow depth, not raw transcription.
- **Customer-tier ambiguity:** the disclosed 3,000+ customer figure likely spans a wide range of account sizes; HCP's revenue model uses a narrower paying-enterprise-account assumption specifically to avoid overstating monetizable scale. Require an ARR-by-tier breakdown in diligence.
- **Long path to escape velocity:** a 2018 founding to a 2025 Series B is a seven-year build. That patience is a founder-quality signal, but it also means less runway of "new category, new investors flooding in" tailwind remains relative to earlier entrants.

## 70. Kick

**Stage:** Series A (HCP characterization; see note below)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://www.kick.co/) | [Seed financing](https://www.axios.com/pro/fintech-deals/2024/10/17/bookkeeping-startup-kick-9-million-ai) | [Follow-on funding](https://medium.com/kickfinance/kick-raises-to-build-the-accounting-firm-of-the-future-10af7f38cabf)

**Stage note:** Kick raised a $9m seed in October 2024 (Axios) and a further round that brought cumulative funding to $20m, announced November 3, 2025, led by Felicis and GV with continued participation from General Catalyst and the OpenAI Startup Fund. No source reviewed explicitly labels the November 2025 round "Series A" — coverage calls it simply "a new funding round." HCP treats it as a de facto Series A for underwriting purposes and flags the label as unconfirmed.

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Conrad Wadowski | Founder | Publishes Kick's funding announcements under the Kick Finance Medium publication; identified as founder in Axios's October 2024 seed coverage. |

### Product description

Kick is a self-driving bookkeeping platform for small businesses, solopreneurs, and the accounting firms that serve them. It auto-categorizes transactions, matches receipts, and produces profit-and-loss and balance-sheet reporting across four tiers: a free plan for new businesses and sole proprietors (250 transactions/year), a $40/month Basic plan with unlimited transactions and automation tooling (including MCP/CLI access for AI agents), a $100/month Plus plan adding multi-entity support and AR/AP automation, and a custom Advanced plan with migration support, dedicated service, and consolidation. The product integrates with Plaid, Stripe, PayPal, Mercury, Ramp, and Gusto, and serves more than 3,000 businesses.

### Thesis: why invest

Kick raised a $9m seed in October 2024 backed by General Catalyst and the OpenAI Startup Fund, plus a long roster of operator angels (Ramp's Eric Glyman and Karim Atiyeh, Gumroad's Sahil Lavingia, ex-Stripe's Lachy Groom, among 60+ others). A further raise brought total funding to $20m by November 2025, adding Felicis and GV. The bookkeeping-automation category has a well-known cautionary precedent — Bench shut down in December 2024 after raising over $100m — which makes Kick's continued investor support and 3,000+ business base a meaningful signal that the current AI-native approach is working where a more manual, human-in-the-loop model failed.

The moat, if it exists, is depth of automated categorization and the MCP/CLI layer that lets accounting firms and power users build automation on top of Kick directly — a wedge toward becoming infrastructure for accounting firms serving many small-business clients, not just a single-user bookkeeping app.

**What must be true:** categorization accuracy must stay high enough to avoid the support-cost spiral that contributed to Bench's collapse; the accounting-firm reseller motion must materialize into a distinct, defensible channel; and gross margin must hold as the customer base scales into more complex, multi-entity accounts.

**Next-round milestones:** 15,000+ businesses served, $25m ARR, gross margin above 70%, at least 50 accounting firms actively reselling Kick to clients, and demonstrated retention through a full annual tax cycle.

### Founder bet

Wadowski is building in a category with a recent, well-publicized failure (Bench), which cuts both ways: it validates unmet demand for automated bookkeeping while raising the bar on unit economics and support costs that any successor must clear. The bet is that AI-native categorization and agent-accessible tooling (MCP/CLI) can achieve the automation ratio Bench's more manual model could not. HCP has not identified independent verification of Wadowski's prior operating background in sources reviewed; confirm this directly in diligence.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$120m** | HCP base case |

|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|

| Illustrative businesses served | 4,000 | 7,500 | 13,000 | 20,000 | 29,000 | 38,000 | 48,000 |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Category precedent:** Bench's shutdown after raising over $100m shows this category can fail even with real usage. Underwrite support cost per account and categorization-error rate specifically, not just top-line growth.
- **Thin founder disclosure:** only one founder is publicly named. Confirm the full founding and leadership team before committing.
- **Commoditization:** QuickBooks Live is bundled distribution from the category's dominant incumbent. Kick must win on automation quality or the accounting-firm channel, not on brand.
- **Round-label ambiguity:** the current round is not clearly labeled Series A in public sources, and the post-money is an HCP assumption. Confirm actual terms before finalizing a check size.

## 71. Formance

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.formance.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.formance.com/blog/company/formance-secures-21-million-dollar-in-series-a-funding-co-led-by-paypal-ventures-and-portage-ventures-to-expand-its-open-source-financial-infrastructure) | [TechCrunch coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2025/01/29/formance-raises-21-million-to-build-the-aws-of-fintech-infrastructure/) | [GitHub](https://github.com/formancehq/ledger)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Clément Salaün | Co-founder | TechCrunch reports his prior role as payments lead at Selency, a French secondhand-furniture marketplace. |
| Anne-Sybille Pradelles | Co-founder | TechCrunch reports her prior role as COO of cybersecurity startup Alsid. |

### Product description

Formance is an open-source, programmable core ledger for fintech and regulated financial companies. Its Ledger module models transactions and balances using Numscript, a purpose-built scripting language for complex financial flows such as multi-party splits and holds. Connectivity ingests transaction data across banks, payment rails, wallets, and exchanges into one unified model; Flows automates fund-lifecycle steps like holds, KYC checks, and payout orchestration; and Reconciliation automatically matches internal ledger records against external bank and processor statements. The core is open source and can be self-hosted, which the company positions as a control-and-transparency advantage over closed, vendor-hosted ledger products. Named customers include Liberis (lending), Doctolib (healthcare payments), Payflip, Shares, Bastion, GetMomo, and Stables. Formance holds SOC 2 Type II and ISO 27001 certifications and states DORA compliance.

### Thesis: why invest

Every fintech eventually needs a ledger that can reconcile money across multiple rails and partners, and most build one in-house — a slow, expensive, and error-prone undertaking. Formance's open-source-plus-managed-cloud model mirrors the pattern that has worked for other infrastructure categories (databases, observability): give developers a credible, inspectable core for free, then monetize the hosted, supported version. The January 2025 $21m Series A was co-led by PayPal Ventures and Portage Ventures, with Y Combinator, Hoxton Ventures, and Axeleo Capital participating — a strong signal, since PayPal Ventures' participation implies real technical and strategic diligence from a company that operates ledgers at enormous scale itself. TechCrunch reported the round came alongside a 10x revenue increase over the prior 12 months, a strong (if narrow, single-data-point) growth signal.

The moat is the same one Mem0 and other open-core infrastructure plays rely on: distribution through open-source adoption, monetization through a hosted control plane, and switching cost that rises as more of a customer's transaction and reconciliation logic lives inside Formance's ledger.

**What must be true:** open-source adoption must convert into paid hosted/enterprise revenue at a healthy rate, not just free self-hosted usage; the 10x growth rate must be sustainable off a larger base, not a one-time step from a very small starting point; and Formance must win regulated-institution trust (SOC 2, ISO 27001, DORA) against both in-house builds and closed competitors like Modern Treasury and Unit.

**Next-round milestones:** $12m-$15m ARR, 15-plus enterprise/regulated-institution customers beyond the current named list, net revenue retention above 120%, and continued open-source community growth (GitHub stars, contributors) as a leading indicator of the top of the funnel.

### Founder bet

Salaün's payments-operations background (Selency) and Pradelles' security/compliance background (Alsid) is a sensible pairing for a ledger product that must be both developer-friendly and audit-grade. The bet is that this team can convert genuinely strong 2024-2025 momentum (10x revenue growth, PayPal Ventures co-lead) into a durable enterprise motion without losing the open-source developer trust that seeded its early adoption.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $100m, HCP assumption |

| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $167m / 2.0x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($100.2m) at 1.0x floor = $100.2m EV, $1.63m proceeds, 0.65x — a capital-loss scenario. Upside detail: 150% of base revenue ($250.5m) at one turn more (3.0x) = $751.5m EV, $12.21m proceeds, 4.88x.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Open-source monetization risk:** self-hosted adopters may never convert to the paid hosted tier. Require cohort data on self-hosted-to-cloud conversion before finalizing valuation.
- **Full entry pricing:** at the $100m HCP assumed post-money (consistent with a roughly 4.75x multiple on the disclosed $21m raise), base MOIC is a modest 2.17x. Invest because PayPal Ventures' co-lead and the disclosed 10x revenue growth are unusually strong signals for this stage — but push for a lower effective entry price or a secondary discount given the full pricing.
- **Narrow growth data point:** "10x revenue growth" off an undisclosed (likely very small) base is a weak standalone signal. Require the absolute revenue figures behind that percentage.
- **Regulated-customer trust:** ledger infrastructure sits in a highly sensitive part of a regulated institution's stack. SOC 2/ISO 27001/DORA compliance is necessary but not sufficient — require reference calls with at least two regulated customers (e.g., Doctolib, Liberis) on reliability and audit experience.

## 72. Texture

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.25m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://www.texturehq.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.texturehq.com/blog/texture-series-a) | [Financing coverage](https://www.powermag.com/texture-raises-12-5m-to-tackle-the-operational-complexity-of-the-modern-grid/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Sanjiv Sanghavi | Co-founder and CEO | Identified by name and title in the company's own Series A blog post. |
| Additional co-founders | Undisclosed | The company's Series A post references two additional co-founders by first name only ("Nick" and "Victor"); full names, surnames, and titles were not independently verifiable in public sources within this session. Confirm in diligence. |

### Product description

Texture describes itself as "the operating system for energy" for utilities, positioning itself around two core capabilities: grid visibility (a single view of every meter, device, and data source on a utility's network, including outage detection and transformer load tracking) and grid operations (load shifting, asset dispatch, and flexibility/demand-response program management). The platform integrates with OEM and energy-data partners including Tesla, FranklinWH, Honeywell, Ecobee, SolarEdge, Leap Energy, and WattTime, and has completed SOC 2 Type I and Type II certification. Disclosed customers include Vermont Electric Cooperative and sonnen (a virtual-power-plant operator managing residential batteries).

### Thesis: why invest

Texture raised a $12.5m Series A in May 2026, co-led by VoLo Earth Ventures and Equal Ventures with Lerer Hippeau and Abstract Ventures increasing their positions, bringing total disclosed funding to approximately $23m. Alongside the round, Texture announced a partnership with NRTC (National Rural Telecommunications Cooperative), whose network represents 850 utility cooperatives nationwide — a distribution channel that could meaningfully accelerate customer acquisition among smaller utilities that lack the budget or staff for enterprise DERMS (distributed energy resource management system) deployments from legacy vendors.

The moat, if defensible, is integration breadth across a highly fragmented device and data landscape (dozens of battery, solar, thermostat, and EV-charging OEMs, each with different APIs) combined with SOC 2-certified reliability that utilities require before connecting Texture to grid-operations workflows. Smaller utilities and co-ops are underserved by legacy DERMS vendors built for large investor-owned utilities, and the NRTC partnership gives Texture a distribution shortcut into exactly that underserved segment.

**What must be true:** device and OEM integration breadth must keep expanding as new DER hardware categories (batteries, EV chargers, smart thermostats, water heaters) proliferate; the NRTC channel must convert into meaningful paid utility/co-op deployments rather than remaining a pilot-stage partnership; and Texture must prove grid-operations reliability at a level utilities trust for real-time dispatch, not just visibility and monitoring.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed ARR (currently undisclosed), 50+ paying utility/co-op customers (beyond pilots), measurable NRTC-channel conversion, and at least one published case study quantifying outage-detection or load-shifting impact.

### Founder bet

The bet is on a founding team building integration-heavy grid software for a segment (utility cooperatives and smaller municipal utilities) that legacy DERMS vendors have largely underserved, with an early distribution partnership (NRTC) that could be a meaningful unlock if it converts to paid deployments. Diligence should confirm the full founding-team roster and titles (only the CEO is named in available public sources), current ARR, and the commercial terms of the NRTC partnership.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **DER-sector multiple compression:** public DER-adjacent comps (Stem, Enphase, Itron) all trade at modest multiples after a difficult 2023-2025 stretch for the sector. Invest only if diligence confirms Texture's pure-software, utility-subscription model (rather than hardware sales) genuinely commands a premium to these hardware-exposed peers.
- **Incomplete founder disclosure:** only the CEO is named in public sources; two additional co-founders are referenced by first name only. Require full leadership roster, equity ownership, and titles before finalizing terms.
- **Channel-conversion risk:** the NRTC partnership covers 850 co-ops but is new (announced with the Series A); it may take years to convert into meaningful paid deployments, and co-ops are typically slow, budget-constrained buyers. Track paid-conversion rate from the NRTC channel explicitly as a milestone.
- **Downside scenario shows capital loss:** at HCP's base assumptions, a below-case outcome (60% of base revenue, one turn off the multiple) produces a MOIC below 1.0x. Require evidence of gross margin and utility-sales-cycle length before committing capital at the proposed valuation.

## 73. Artisan

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://www.artisan.co/) | [Series A financing](https://techcrunch.com/2025/04/09/artisan-the-stop-hiring-humans-ai-agent-startup-raises-25m-and-is-still-hiring-humans/) | [Company announcement](https://www.artisan.co/blog/artisan-series-a)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Jaspar Carmichael-Jack | Co-founder and CEO | Named in TechCrunch's April 2025 Series A coverage and Artisan's own announcement as the company's CEO and public spokesperson. |
| Additional co-founders | Undisclosed | Public sources reviewed name only Carmichael-Jack; Artisan's Series A announcement separately introduces Ming Li (ex-Deel VP of Technology) as CTO, hired after the raise rather than as a founder. Confirm full founding-team composition in diligence. |

### Product description

Artisan builds "AI employees" — branded, purpose-specific agents — starting with Ava, an AI Business Development Representative. Ava identifies leads, researches them using a real-time context engine that scrapes the web for buying signals (job changes, new funding, leadership moves), writes and sends personalized outreach across email and social channels, and books meetings, all without human SDRs in the loop. Artisan is building two additional agents: Aaron (inbound-lead qualification) and Aria (meeting scheduling and summaries). SumUp is a named customer, reporting 8-15 positive replies per week from hard-to-reach SMB prospects using Ava.

### Thesis: why invest

Artisan raised a $25m Series A in April 2025 led by Glade Brook Capital, with HubSpot Ventures, Oliver Jung, Day One Ventures, BOND, Soma Capital, Sequoia Scout, and Y Combinator participating — notably including HubSpot Ventures, a strategic investor from the CRM incumbent whose customer base Artisan's product complements. At the time of the raise, Artisan reported $5m in ARR and 250 paying companies as customers, and had hired a former Deel VP of Technology (with four senior engineers from Rippling) as CTO, suggesting a deliberate scale-up of engineering leadership post-raise.

The "AI employee" framing and multi-agent roadmap (Ava, Aaron, Aria) is a bet that outbound sales automation is the wedge into a broader autonomous-workforce platform, not the end state. If Artisan can cross-sell Aaron and Aria into its existing Ava customer base, net revenue retention could compound faster than new-logo growth alone.

**What must be true:** outbound email/social deliverability and reply quality must hold up as AI-generated outreach volume scales industry-wide (a rising deliverability and spam-filter risk for the whole category); Aaron and Aria must actually ship and attach to the existing base; and Artisan must differentiate from a large and growing set of AI SDR competitors on outcomes, not just positioning.

**Next-round milestones:** $20m+ ARR, 600+ customers, net revenue retention above 120% driven by multi-agent attach, published reply-rate or pipeline benchmarks versus human SDR baselines, and evidence Aaron/Aria are live and monetizing.

### Founder bet

Carmichael-Jack's public profile centers on the "stop hiring humans" positioning that generated significant press attention at the Series A; the substantive signal for HCP is the $5m ARR and 250-customer base already in place at the round, plus the post-raise hire of an experienced CTO from Deel/Rippling to build out the technical organization. The founding team beyond Carmichael-Jack is not established in sources reviewed and should be confirmed directly.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Category crowding:** 11x, Regie.ai, and numerous other AI SDR tools are chasing the same buyer with similar pitches. Artisan's differentiation must be measured in reply/meeting-booked outcomes, not positioning.
- **Deliverability risk:** as AI-generated outbound volume rises industry-wide, email and social platforms are tightening spam and authenticity filters, which could compress Ava's core value proposition for everyone in the category simultaneously.
- **Thin founding-team disclosure:** only one founder is publicly confirmed. Confirm the full team and equity structure in diligence.

## 74. Numeric

**Stage:** Series B (verified; roster hint said Series A). Numeric priced a $28m Series A in October 2024, then a $51m Series B on November 19, 2025; HCP keeps Numeric in scope per the batch's Series-B exception.
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.numeric.io/) | [Series A financing](https://techcrunch.com/2024/10/10/numeric-grabs-28m-series-a-for-automating-accounting-with-ai/) | [Series B announcement](https://www.numeric.io/blog/numeric-raises-51m-series-b)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Parker Gilbert | Co-founder | Prior VP of Finance experience at Hearth, per Numeric's own Series B announcement; brings direct accounting-operator background to the founding team. |
| Anthony Alvernaz | Co-founder | Named alongside Gilbert and Bihl in TechCrunch's October 2024 Series A coverage; specific role and background not detailed beyond co-founder status in sources reviewed. |
| Andrew Bihl | Co-founder | Named alongside Gilbert and Alvernaz in TechCrunch's October 2024 Series A coverage; specific role and background not detailed beyond co-founder status in sources reviewed. |

### Product description

Numeric is an AI-powered close-automation platform for enterprise and mid-market accounting teams, unifying close management, cash reconciliation, and reporting into one system. Its cash-management module automates more than 90% of cash matching and journal entries across bank integrations; its analytics suite generates flux analysis, CFO-ready reporting, and AI-written variance explanations, and includes an MCP connector for building custom agents on top of the platform. Numeric is expanding from close management into a broader "compound startup" finance-data platform, with additional products planned through 2026 and 2027. Customers include Brex, Plaid, Wealthfront, Public.com, Stash, Riskified (NYSE: RSKD), Asana, and Parafin.

### Thesis: why invest

Numeric raised a $28m Series A in October 2024 led by Menlo Ventures with IVP and Socii joining, five months after a $10m seed; revenue had grown 4x to the "single-digit millions" heading into that round. It then raised a $51m Series B on November 19, 2025, led by IVP with Menlo Ventures, Founders Fund, Alkeon, 8VC, Socii Capital, Access Industries, and others returning or joining, plus operator angels including former BlackLine CEO Marc Huffman and former NetSuite CFO Ron Gill — a strong signal of finance-industry insider conviction. Total funding is $89m. Customer-reported outcomes are concrete: Brex cut its close timeline 33%, Public.com tripled team output, and DailyPay reported 80% of flux-analysis first drafts now AI-written.

The moat is depth inside the close cycle: once a controller's team routes reconciliation, variance analysis, and reporting through Numeric, switching costs rise with every additional bank connection, close checklist, and historical variance explanation stored in the system. Expansion beyond close into a "unified financial data layer" would extend that lock-in further.

**What must be true:** the platform-expansion roadmap (beyond close management) must land with existing customers rather than diluting focus; net revenue retention must stay strong as Numeric moves upmarket into more complex enterprise accounts; and the actual Series B valuation (undisclosed) must not be so far above HCP's assumption that ownership is not worth the check.

**Next-round milestones:** $40m+ ARR, net revenue retention above 130%, at least 15 reference customers above $250k ACV, and at least one additional product beyond close management in general availability with paying customers.

### Founder bet

The founding team combines a direct accounting-operator background (Gilbert's VP of Finance experience at Hearth) with two co-founders whose specific backgrounds are not detailed in sources reviewed. The strongest external validation is the operator-angel bench at the Series B — a former BlackLine CEO and a former NetSuite CFO both investing suggests informed insiders believe Numeric's product genuinely displaces or extends the tools they used to run.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Enterprise (>$500m revenue) companies | 3,000 | $150,000 | $450m | HCP assumption: full close, cash, and reporting suite |
| Mid-market ($50m-$500m revenue) companies | 15,000 | $30,000 | $450m | HCP assumption |
| Emerging / high-growth startups | 20,000 | $10,000 | $200m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | 38,000 | | **$1.10bn** | Annual enterprise close-automation software pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **29.1% of TAM revenue** | Reflects strong existing enterprise logos (Brex, OpenAI, Plaid, Wealthfront) |

| Exit enterprise value | $960m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $4.8m / **1.92x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.77x / 3.84x |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Valuation opacity:** the Series B post-money is undisclosed; HCP's $350m assumption drives the return math directly. A materially higher actual price would push MOIC toward the Basis/Eve range. Confirm terms before committing.
- **Platform-expansion distraction:** moving from a focused close-automation product to a broader finance-data platform risks diluting the product that earned Brex, Plaid, and Wealthfront as customers. Track close-product NRR separately from new-module attach.
- **Incumbent response:** BlackLine and Workiva have large installed bases and could add AI-native variance analysis directly. Numeric's edge must be measured against feature parity timelines, not just current capability gaps.
- **Enterprise sales cycle risk:** moving upmarket into larger enterprise accounts lengthens sales cycles and raises implementation cost. Track time-to-value and services-attach rate by cohort.

---

## 75. Kudos

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://joinkudos.com) | [Series A coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2024/05/17/kudos-ai-smart-wallet-10m-credit-card/) | [Finextra coverage](https://www.finextra.com/newsarticle/44168/kudos-raises-102m-for-ai-powered-smart-wallet)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Tikue Anazodo | Co-founder and CEO | TechCrunch reports prior roles at Google and Affirm alongside co-founder Ismail. |
| Ahmad Ismail | Co-founder | Same Google/Affirm background per TechCrunch. |

### Product description

Kudos is an AI-powered smart wallet — a browser extension and app — that recommends which credit card a user should use for a given purchase to maximize rewards or cash back. Its "MariaGPT" tool indexes and compares more than 3,000 cards; "Dream Wallet" gives personalized card recommendations based on a user's actual spending; and "Kudos Boost" layers additional cash-back rewards on top of a user's existing card rewards across more than 15,000 partner retailers. The company monetizes primarily through affiliate/referral economics on card recommendations and partner cash-back deals, with plans (per the Series A announcement) to expand MariaGPT into a general personal-finance assistant and a points-based flight-booking portal.

### Thesis: why invest

Consumers leave real money on the table by using the wrong card for a given purchase, and Kudos turns that into a lightweight, checkout-adjacent recommendation product. The May 2024 $10.2m Series A was led by QED Investors, with Patron, Samsung Next, SV Angel, Precursor Ventures, and individual investors including The Points Guy founder Brian Kelly. The company reported growth from 1,000 beta testers in 2022 to 200,000 registered users and over $200m in annualized checkout GMV by the Series A.

The moat is potentially the combination of spend data and card-recommendation accuracy — the more purchase history Kudos sees, the better its recommendations, and better recommendations drive more checkout volume through its extension. However, TechCrunch's own reporting characterized Kudos as "still in the early stages of revenue generation" at the time of the Series A, which is a meaningful company-and-reporter-acknowledged gap between usage and monetization that HCP has not seen closed in more recent public disclosures.

**What must be true:** referral/affiliate economics must scale into durable, high-margin revenue rather than one-time bonuses; the recommendation engine's data advantage must be defensible against card issuers and comparison sites building similar tools natively; and Kudos must convert its 200,000-plus registered users into a meaningfully monetized cohort, not just an engaged-but-unmonetized one.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed revenue run rate (not just GMV) in the $10m-$15m range, evidence that MariaGPT/Dream Wallet materially improves conversion or retention versus the base extension, and clear separation from free comparison-site competitors on defensibility.

### Founder bet

Anazodo and Ismail's shared Google/Affirm background is a credible signal for both consumer-product execution and fintech-specific judgment. The open question, consistent with TechCrunch's own framing, is whether Kudos can convert genuine user engagement (36% month-over-month growth and 90% retention reported in 2022) into revenue at a pace that justifies the Series A valuation step-up, which the company itself described only as "more than double its seed valuation" without a figure.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|
| Card-holding U.S. consumers open to optimization tools | 60m | $5 | $300m | HCP assumption |
| Affluent/power multi-card users | 15m | $15 | $225m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$525m** | Annual referral/affiliate revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **18.1%** | ~9.5m monetized users by 2032 |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$95m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Registered users | 400k | 900k | 1.8m | 3.2m | 5.0m | 7.0m | 9.5m |
| Net annual revenue/user | $2 | $3 | $4 | $5.5 | $7 | $8.5 | $10 |
| **Revenue, $m** | **1** | **3** | **7** | **18** | **35** | **60** | **95** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Kudos** | AI card-recommendation smart wallet | X card selection recommendation; X cash-back layer; Partial general finance assistant | Browser extension, app | Spend-data-driven recommendation accuracy | Free consumer product; monetized via affiliate/referral | $10.2m Series A; $17.2m total; valuation undisclosed; QED, Patron, Samsung Next |
| NerdWallet | Personal-finance comparison/media | X card/product comparison content; Partial real-time checkout recommendation | Web/app, media-driven | SEO/content scale and brand trust | Referral/advertising | Public |
| MaxRewards | Card-optimization app | X card recommendation and reward tracking; Partial cash-back layer | App | Early-mover consumer app in category | Freemium subscription | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Extend | Virtual card management for rewards optimization | Partial card selection; X virtual card issuance | App | Issuer partnerships for virtual cards | Freemium | Private; valuation not used |
| The Points Guy | Points/rewards media and tools | Partial card comparison content; No evidence real-time checkout recommendation | Web/media | Brand and content authority | Advertising/affiliate | Private (Red Ventures); capital not comparable |
| Credit Karma | Consumer credit and card recommendation | X card recommendation at scale; Partial checkout-time integration | App/web | Massive user base and credit-data access | Referral/advertising | Private (Intuit subsidiary) |
| Bankrate | Financial product comparison | Partial card comparison; No evidence AI checkout recommendation | Web | Scale and SEO | Advertising/referral | Public (Red Ventures majority-owned) |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [NerdWallet](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/nrds/statistics/) | 0.68x | Closest business-model comp: referral/comparison monetization |
| [SoFi](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/sofi/statistics/) | 5.25x | Consumer fintech at scale (reused from reference file) |
| [Robinhood](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/hood/statistics/) | 18.29x | Premium-growth consumer fintech (reused from reference file) |
| **Median** | **5.25x** | HCP uses 1.5x, close to NerdWallet given Kudos's own admitted early revenue stage |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $50m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 4.00% |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($57m) at 1.0x floor = $57m EV, $1.48m proceeds, 0.74x — a capital-loss scenario. Upside detail: 150% of base revenue ($142.5m) at 2.5x = $356.25m EV, $9.26m proceeds, 4.63x.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Revenue behind usage:** the company's own Series A reporting acknowledged early-stage revenue generation relative to 200,000-plus users and $200m-plus GMV. Require a current revenue disclosure before advancing past Watch.
- **Category crowding:** NerdWallet, Credit Karma, MaxRewards, and Extend all compete for the same card-optimization wedge, several with far larger distribution.
- **Defensibility of the data edge:** card issuers themselves could build native recommendation features, eroding a third-party wallet's advantage.
- **Reconsideration path:** a disclosed revenue run rate materially above the early-2024 characterization, or a lower effective entry price, would justify moving to Diligence.

## 76. HappyRobot

**Stage:** Series B (verified; roster hint said Series A). HappyRobot priced a $15.6m Series A in December 2024, then a $44m Series B on approximately September 2025; HCP keeps HappyRobot in scope per the batch's Series-B exception.
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.happyrobot.ai/) | [Series A financing](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/happyrobot-raises-15-6-million-series-a-funding-led-by-a16z-to-transform-logistics-with-agentic-ai-302322662.html) | [Series B coverage](https://techfundingnews.com/happyrobot-44m-series-b-ai-workforce-supply-chain/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Pablo | Co-founder and CEO | HappyRobot's own Series A announcement identifies "Pablo" (AI research background) as CEO; full surname not given in the source reviewed. |
| Luis | Co-founder and CTO | Identified in the same announcement (AI research background) as CTO; full surname not given in the source reviewed. |
| Javi | Co-founder and COO | Identified in the same announcement, with shipper-side logistics operating experience; full surname not given in the source reviewed. |

Full legal names, prior companies, and detailed backgrounds for all three founders should be confirmed directly in diligence — HappyRobot's own public financing material refers to them by first name only.

### Product description

HappyRobot is an agentic AI platform that deploys "AI workers" to automate phone-based and multi-channel communication across supply-chain and enterprise operations. Agents handle inbound and outbound carrier sales calls, check calls, proof-of-delivery collection, and now extend beyond logistics into customer support, sales, finance, and HR/recruiting functions across industries including utilities, airlines, retail, manufacturing, insurance, and financial services. The platform includes a governance layer (behavioral evaluation, adversarial testing, audits) and holds SOC 2, GDPR, HIPAA, EU AI Act, NIST CSF, and DORA compliance credentials. The company reports 150+ enterprise customers, including DHL, Kuehne+Nagel, Ryder, Schneider, Werner, Naturgy, CMA CGM, and Uber Freight.

### Thesis: why invest

HappyRobot raised a $15.6m Series A in December 2024 led by a16z with RyderVentures (a strategic investor from a named customer) participating, following seed funding from Array Ventures and Y Combinator. It then closed a $44m Series B roughly ten months later, led by Base10 Partners with a16z, Array Ventures, Avra, Samsara Ventures, Tokio Marine, WiL, and YC participating; TechFundingNews reported the round valued the company at approximately $500m — a third-party estimate HCP treats as directional, not confirmed. Total disclosed funding is $62m. The company reports 10x revenue growth around the Series B and has expanded from a freight-brokerage-specific wedge into a broader cross-industry "AI workforce" platform.

The original moat was logistics-specific: freight communication is high-volume, repetitive, and phone-native, making it a strong fit for voice AI with measurable ROI (reported 50% call-time reduction, one-third lower operational cost). Expanding beyond logistics into utilities, airlines, and financial services broadens the addressable base but also increases competitive surface area against general-purpose voice-AI infrastructure providers.

**What must be true:** the platform must retain its logistics-specific performance edge (integration depth with freight systems, domain-tuned conversation flows) even as it generalizes horizontally; cross-industry expansion must not dilute the product quality that won DHL, Schneider, and Uber Freight; and the reported ~$500m valuation must not already price in most of the achievable multi-year growth.

**Next-round milestones:** 300+ enterprise customers, $40m+ ARR, expansion revenue from existing logos into new functions (beyond carrier communication) exceeding 25% of total revenue, and confirmed, audited Series B terms.

### Founder bet

The founding team pairs two AI-research backgrounds (Pablo, Luis) with direct shipper-side logistics operating experience (Javi) — a sensible split between technical build and domain credibility for the initial freight wedge. The horizontal expansion into utilities, airlines, and financial services tests whether that domain-specific advantage generalizes, or whether HappyRobot becomes a more commoditized voice-AI infrastructure player competing with well-funded horizontal entrants. Confirm full names and prior company history in diligence; public materials reviewed use first names only.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Large freight brokers / 3PLs (revenue >$100m) | 800 | $200,000 | $160m | HCP assumption |
| Mid-size brokers / carriers | 8,000 | $30,000 | $240m | HCP assumption |

### Competitive landscape

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Unconfirmed valuation:** the ~$500m Series B price is third-party reported, not company-disclosed. Confirm actual terms; a materially higher real price would push this toward a Pass, consistent with Basis and Eve in this batch.
- **Freight cyclicality:** freight brokerage end markets are historically cyclical; a downturn in freight volumes could slow HappyRobot's core-vertical growth independent of product quality.
- **Horizontal-expansion dilution risk:** moving into utilities, airlines, and financial services tests whether the freight-specific moat generalizes, or whether HappyRobot ends up competing directly with horizontal voice-AI infrastructure players like Retell and Bland on their own terms.
- **Thin founder disclosure:** company materials name founders by first name only. Confirm full identities, equity ownership, and prior track records in diligence.

## 77. Timeleft

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://timeleft.com/) | [Series A funding record](https://www.trysignalbase.com/news/funding/timeleft-raises-70m-series-a-funding) | [Founder profile](https://www.temy.co/breaking-bread-building-bonds-how-maxime-barbiers-timeleft-is-redefining-connections-in-cities-worldwide/) | [London expansion post](https://timeleft.com/post/timelefts-london-debut-eclectic-dinners-in-the-uks-metropolis/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Maxime Barbier | Co-founder and CEO | A serial entrepreneur profile (Temy) describes Barbier's path through nightlife promotion and media before founding Timeleft; multiple press profiles identify him as the French founder. |
| Adrien de Oliveira | Co-founder | Named as co-founder alongside Barbier in company-adjacent reporting; confirm current operating role in diligence. |

### Product description

Timeleft matches small groups of strangers — typically five to six people — for a recurring weekly dinner, based on a compatibility questionnaire. Events run every Wednesday (with additional formats added over time) in restaurants Timeleft partners with, explicitly positioned as neither a dating app nor a networking app but a tool for building real-world friendship. The service has scaled from a single-city experiment (the first event drew 25 diners) to more than 200 cities across 52 countries by December 2025, per the company's own site, with recent expansions into London and Liverpool. The company reports meaningful, disclosed recurring revenue (see below), which distinguishes it from most other companies in this batch.

### Thesis: why invest

Timeleft raised a $7m Series A in July 2024, with Redstone, EnjoyVenture, Smash Capital, FJ Labs, and Global Founders Capital among its investors, per aggregator and funding-database reporting (HCP could not locate a primary press release for this specific round and flags it for diligence confirmation). Independent reporting (via a founder-profile piece and the company's own posts) states Timeleft reached roughly €18m in annualized recurring revenue and 150,000 monthly dinner participants across 200+ cities by August 2025 — real, disclosed operating scale that is unusual for this batch, where most companies have no public revenue at all.

The loneliness and adult-friendship problem Timeleft addresses is real and widely documented, and the company has found a repeatable, low-cost-to-replicate-per-city format (a recurring Wednesday ritual, matched by algorithm, hosted at partner restaurants) that has scaled to more cities and countries than most consumer social startups reach. The moat is the compatibility-matching data and city-by-city operating playbook (restaurant partnerships, local marketing, safety protocols) built over roughly 200 city launches — a genuine execution asset that is hard to replicate quickly.

**What must be true:** growth must continue converting into paying, repeat participants rather than one-time novelty-seekers; the restaurant-partner network must scale without service-quality dilution; and the recurring-dinner format must retain differentiation as competitors (Pie, 222, and others in this batch) enter the same broad "IRL loneliness" category.

**Next-round milestones:** $30m+ annualized revenue in USD terms, disclosed repeat-participation and retention rates, profitability or a clear path to it at the city level, and continued expansion into major markets (Asia-Pacific, per the company's stated goals) without diluting per-city unit economics.

### Founder bet

Barbier's path — nightlife promotion, then media, then Timeleft — reads as a founder who repeatedly tests ideas against real audience response rather than a single long-held thesis; the Temy profile frames the first Timeleft dinner (25 diners) growing through successive events (35, 70, 81 participants) as exactly that kind of iterative, feedback-driven build. That pattern is a plausible explanation for how a small founding team reached 200+ cities faster than better-funded competitors in this batch. Diligence should confirm de Oliveira's current operating scope and assess how much of the city-expansion playbook is genuinely repeatable versus founder-dependent.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Global urban adults 25–45 willing to pay for scheduled social dining | 70m | $30 | $2.10bn | HCP assumption: major-metro subset across Timeleft's live and planned markets |
| Corporate/community partnership layer | — | — | $150m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$2.25bn** | Annual net-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **8.2% of TAM revenue** | Roughly consistent with continued multi-year expansion from the disclosed 150,000-monthly-participant base |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$185m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **24** | **45** | **75** | **110** | **145** | **165** | **185** |

The 2026E figure of $24m reflects modest continued growth off the disclosed ~€18m (~$19–20m USD, HCP FX assumption) run rate reported for August 2025.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Timeleft** | Scheduled stranger-dinner matching | X matching, scheduling, restaurant partnerships | Mobile app, weekly recurring in-person events | 200+-city operating playbook and compatibility-matching data | Per-event fee; exact pricing undisclosed | $7m Series A (reported); total and valuation undisclosed; Redstone, EnjoyVenture, Smash Capital, FJ Labs, Global Founders Capital |
| 222 | AI-matched curated experiences (dinners, comedy) | X matching and event booking; smaller city footprint | Mobile app | AI personality-assessment matching | Undisclosed | $10.1m Series A; Upfront-led (see this batch's 222 memo) |
| Pie | AI-matched small-group friendship events | X matching; pays organizers to host | Mobile app, 2-city footprint | AI quiz plus paid-organizer guarantee | Undisclosed | $11.5m Series A (see this batch's Pie memo) |
| Meetup | Interest-group event listings | Partial matching (self-selected groups, not algorithmic); X event hosting tools | Web/app | Long-standing installed base and group-organizer network | Subscription (organizer-paid) | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Bumble BFF | Friendship-matching within the Bumble app | Partial matching; X swipe-based discovery | Mobile app | Existing Bumble user base and brand | Freemium/subscription | Public (Bumble Inc.) |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Yelp](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/yelp/statistics/) | 1.01x | Local-discovery/hospitality-adjacent consumer comp |
| [Eventbrite](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/eb/statistics/) | 0.77x | Recurring in-person-event infrastructure comp |
| [Bumble](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/bmbl/statistics/) | 0.85x | Social-matching consumer comp |
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | High-engagement consumer-social comp |
| **Median** | **0.93x** | HCP uses 1.5x, a premium justified by Timeleft's disclosed real revenue growth versus mature/declining comps |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $100m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 2.50% ($2.5m / $100m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 1.625% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $185m / 1.5x |
| Exit enterprise value | $277.5m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $4.51m / **1.80x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.72x / 4.51x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($111m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (1.5x − 1 turn = 0.5x, floored to 1.0x) yields $111m EV, $1.804m proceeds, 0.72x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($277.5m) at 2.5x yields $693.75m EV, $11.27m proceeds, 4.51x MOIC.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **FX exposure:** disclosed revenue is in euros; USD-denominated returns depend on EUR/USD, which the model does not otherwise adjust for. Model both currencies explicitly in diligence.
- **Novelty-to-habit conversion:** rapid city expansion can mask weak repeat-participation in any single city. Require cohort retention data (do participants come back for a 2nd, 5th, 10th dinner?).
- **Restaurant-partner dependency:** service quality and unit economics depend on a fragmented, city-by-city restaurant partner base. Assess partner-renewal and quality-control processes.
- **Category crowding:** Pie, 222, and Bumble BFF are all chasing the same "AI-matched IRL connection" thesis. Timeleft's revenue and city-count lead is real today, but the category has no confirmed long-term winner.

## 78. SchoolAI

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.5m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://schoolai.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2025/04/02/3054126/0/en/SchoolAI-Secures-25-Million-to-Help-Teachers-and-Schools-Reach-Every-Student.html) | [Pricing](https://schoolai.com/pricing)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Caleb Hicks | Founder and CEO | 15-plus years in education as a classroom teacher and product leader, including developing iOS curriculum at Apple and co-founding Lambda School; multiple profiles (PangeaGlobe, BusinessQ) confirm his background and role. |

### Product description

SchoolAI is a K-12 (and some higher-ed) classroom AI platform combining two halves: a "Classroom Experience" of AI assistants that help teachers with lesson prep and administrative work, and "Spaces" — personalized AI tutors, games, and lessons that adapt to individual students' learning styles. The platform is built with explicit compliance positioning: FERPA, COPPA, and SOC 2 Type 2 compliant, 1EdTech certified, and ESSA Level III validated (the last of which qualifies it for Title I, II, III, and IV-A federal education funding, a meaningful go-to-market lever for U.S. public school sales). SchoolAI reports usage in more than 1 million classrooms, across all 50 U.S. states and more than 80 countries, embedded in more than 400 school districts, with over 150,000 distinct AI tools created by educators on the platform.

### Thesis: why invest

SchoolAI closed a $25m Series A in April 2025 led by Insight Partners, with existing investors NextView Ventures, The General Partnership, and Peterson Ventures participating, bringing total funding to $32m. The scale of disclosed usage — 1 million classrooms, 400-plus districts, 80-plus countries — is the largest verified footprint of any company in this batch, and the ESSA Level III validation is a genuine, hard-to-replicate regulatory asset that materially eases procurement inside U.S. public school budgets.

The core tension in this memo is that usage scale is exceptional while the available public-comps set for education software (Duolingo, Coursera, Stride, Chegg) trades at meaningfully lower multiples than most SaaS categories, reflecting real structural concerns about institutional budget cycles and AI-driven disruption of the underlying content-and-tutoring business. SchoolAI must convert its free-tier classroom scale into paid Pro and Scale district contracts to earn a multiple better than the comp set implies; it has clearly won usage, but the public record does not yet demonstrate it has won monetization at a rate consistent with a strong return at the assumed entry price.

**What must be true:** free-tier classroom usage must convert to paid Pro/Scale contracts at a materially higher rate than typical district-software funnels; the ESSA/compliance moat must translate into faster procurement cycles, not just easier initial adoption; and per-district or per-teacher revenue must scale without a linear increase in implementation and support cost.

**Next-round milestones:** $30m ARR, 1,000 paying districts (up from an unknown current paid-district count), net revenue retention above 115%, and a demonstrated reduction in average district sales-cycle length.

### Founder bet

Hicks combines rare direct classroom experience with prior edtech product leadership (Apple, Lambda School), which is a credible foundation for building a product teachers actually adopt rather than merely purchase. As a single named founder at this scale of company, diligence should confirm the depth of the executive team below Hicks and the durability of district relationships beyond any one champion.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| U.S. K-12 teachers (per-teacher paid tier) | 3,800,000 | $200 | $0.76bn | HCP assumption |

### Public comps and exit model

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price versus comp set:** at the $120m post-money HCP assumption, the return math is unattractive unless SchoolAI earns a materially better multiple than its public comp set through demonstrated district retention. Price discipline in the actual round is the single biggest lever HCP controls here.
- **Monetization behind usage:** 1 million classrooms of usage is a remarkable top-of-funnel number, but the company does not disclose paying-district count or ARR. Require both before underwriting further.
- **Institutional sales cycles:** district procurement is slow and budget-constrained; growth assumptions above may prove optimistic relative to real-world K-12 purchasing calendars.
- **Why invest anyway:** the ESSA Level III validation and full compliance stack are genuinely rare and hard for a smaller competitor to replicate quickly, and the disclosed footprint (400+ districts, 80+ countries) suggests SchoolAI may already be a de facto standard in some markets. This is a business worth pursuing at a lower price or with a valuation-protection mechanism, not at the disclosed round's likely terms without further diligence.

## 79. Sereact

**Stage:** Series B (screened at Series A per roster)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://sereact.ai/) | [Series A announcement](https://sereact.ai/posts/sereact-fundraising-series-a) | [Series B report](https://siliconangle.com/2026/04/27/sereact-raises-110m-scale-ai-robotic-brain-expand-us/)

### Stage-progression note

Sereact was assigned to this batch as a Series A company. Since its €25m Series A closed in January 2025, the company has raised a further $110m Series B (April 2026), consistent with the instruction that a company may be retained past Series A when the exception is explained. Because a new HCP check today would price against the most recent round, this memo models entry at Series B economics rather than the original Series A terms.

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Ralf Gulde | Co-founder and CEO | Former AI researcher at the University of Stuttgart; publicly quoted describing Sereact's robots as adapting "to dynamic tasks in real-time" rather than following fixed programming. |
| Marc Tuscher | Co-founder | Former AI researcher at the University of Stuttgart alongside Gulde; co-developed the company's vision-language-action approach to robot control. |

### Product description

Sereact builds hardware-agnostic AI software — described as Vision Language Action Models (VLAM) — that lets industrial and warehouse robots perform tasks they were not explicitly programmed for, by combining visual perception with language-model-style reasoning about how to manipulate objects. Rather than selling robots, Sereact sells the "brain" that runs on top of third-party robot arms already installed at a customer site, positioning it as a software layer across heterogeneous hardware fleets. Disclosed customers include BMW, Daimler Truck, Bol, Active Ants, and MS Direct.

### Thesis: why invest

Sereact is one of the more commercially validated companies in this batch: as of its April 2026 Series B, the company reported more than 200 systems deployed across Europe, more than 1 billion production picks completed, and an intervention rate of roughly 1 in every 53,000 requests requiring remote human help — a genuinely strong reliability signal for autonomous manipulation if independently verified. The Series B was led by Headline VC, with Bullhound Capital, Felix Capital, Daphni, and existing investors Creandum, Air Street Capital, and Point Nine participating, bringing total funding to more than $140m. Proceeds are earmarked for a next-generation "Cortex 2.0" platform and a first U.S. office in Boston.

The moat is real and plausible: a hardware-agnostic software layer with a billion-plus production picks of real-world manipulation data, deployed across marquee automotive and logistics customers (BMW, Daimler Truck), is a genuinely hard data and integration asset to replicate quickly. The problem for this memo is not the business — it is the price. A $110m Series B implies a substantially higher valuation than the January 2025 Series A, and a small $2.0m check now buys a fraction of the ownership it would have at Series A terms.

**What must be true:** system deployment growth must continue at or above the pace implied by 200+ systems in roughly 15 months of commercial operation; the low intervention rate must hold as deployment volume and task diversity scale; and the U.S. expansion must convert into signed enterprise contracts, not just a sales office.

**Next-round milestones:** 500+ deployed systems, disclosed ARR, at least three named U.S. enterprise customers, and continued improvement (or at minimum, no degradation) in the human-intervention rate as scale increases.

### Founder bet

The bet on two Stuttgart AI researchers who built a genuinely differentiated vision-language-action approach and have already proven it at real industrial scale (BMW, Daimler Truck) is a strong one. The issue for a new, small check is not founder quality — it is that the company's own execution has been strong enough to command a price that makes a $1.0m-$2.5m check's return math difficult without an unusually large exit outcome.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Robot cells | Annual software value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Warehouse/3PL robotic cells | 60,000 | $40,000 | $2.40bn | HCP assumption |
| Automotive/industrial manufacturing robotic cells | 25,000 | $70,000 | $1.75bn | HCP assumption |

| Avg. annual software revenue/system | $55k | $60k | $65k | $70k | $75k | $78k | $80k |

### Competitive landscape

| Physical Intelligence | General-purpose robot foundation models | X general manipulation research; Partial commercial deployment breadth | Model + partner hardware | Foundation-model research talent and capital | Undisclosed | Private; large late-stage rounds; valuation not used here |

### Public comps and exit model

|---|---:|---|
| [Cognex](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/cgnx/statistics/) | 9.97x | Machine-vision software/hardware for manipulation |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price:** at an assumed $550m post-money, a $2.0m check clears only a modest base MOIC and a sub-1.0x downside. Invest only with a materially lower effective entry — a secondary at a discount, a side letter, or a larger allocation that changes the fund's negotiating position.
- **Deployment claims require verification:** the 1-in-53,000 intervention rate and 1 billion picks are company-reported figures; request raw deployment logs or a customer reference call before underwriting off them.
- **Hardware-vendor bundling:** ABB, Fanuc, and KUKA could bundle equivalent AI control software with their own arms, undercutting Sereact's hardware-agnostic pitch. Sereact's cross-vendor data advantage is the defense, but it must keep expanding faster than incumbents can copy.
- **U.S. expansion execution:** a new Boston office is not the same as U.S. revenue. Require signed U.S. contracts, not office headcount, as the milestone that matters.
