## 80. Cargado

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://cargado.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://cargado.com/news) | [FreightWaves coverage](https://www.freightwaves.com/news/exclusive-cargado-raises-12m-to-boost-cross-border-trucking-marketplace)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Matt Silver | Co-founder | FreightWaves and the company's own Series A materials identify Silver as co-founder; company founded in January 2024. Exact current title not confirmed; confirm in diligence. |
| Rylan Hawkins | Co-founder | FreightWaves and the company's own Series A materials identify Hawkins as co-founder alongside Silver. Exact current title not confirmed; confirm in diligence. |

### Product description

Cargado operates an invite-only load board for cross-border U.S.-Mexico trucking freight. Brokers, 3PLs, and freight forwarders post cross-border loads and receive bids from a vetted network of cross-border trucking companies; the company personally vets every carrier before granting marketplace access, addressing a real trust and fraud problem in cross-border freight where carrier legitimacy and customs compliance are harder to verify than in domestic U.S. trucking. At the time of its Series A, Cargado reported more than 200 broker/3PL/forwarder customers and more than 650 vetted cross-border carriers, achieved within roughly six months of public launch.

### Thesis: why invest

Cargado raised a $12m Series A in April 2025, led by LGVP with Conversion Capital, Assembly Ventures, and Friends & Family Capital joining as new investors alongside existing investors Primary Venture Partners, Ironspring Ventures, Zenda Capital, and Proeza Ventures. U.S.-Mexico cross-border trucking is a large, structurally growing freight corridor as nearshoring shifts manufacturing toward Mexico, and it is underserved by modern digital marketplaces relative to domestic U.S. freight, which DAT, Uber Freight, and others have already digitized. Cargado's carrier-vetting process directly addresses a documented pain point (customs fraud, unreliable cross-border carriers) that generic domestic load boards do not solve.

The moat, if it holds, is the vetted carrier network itself and the trust and performance data accumulated across it — a two-sided network where both broker-side demand and vetted-carrier supply reinforce each other. The company's rapid growth (200+ customers and 650+ carriers within six months of launch) is a genuine positive signal of product-market fit in a specific niche.

**What must be true:** the vetted-carrier network must remain meaningfully more trustworthy than open load boards as it scales, without vetting quality degrading; take rate or monetization per load must expand beyond simple brokerage matching into higher-margin services (factoring, insurance, customs, financing) to escape freight brokerage's structurally thin public-market multiples; and Cargado must defend its position against Nuvocargo, a well-funded direct competitor targeting the same corridor.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed net revenue/take rate, 1,500+ vetted carriers, expansion into at least one adjacent monetization line (factoring, customs brokerage, or insurance), and evidence that carrier and broker retention remain high as the network scales past its initial cohort.

### Founder bet

The bet is on two founders who identified a specific, underserved corridor (U.S.-Mexico cross-border trucking) and built rapid two-sided marketplace liquidity within six months of launch. Diligence should focus on unit economics per load (take rate net of vetting/compliance cost), customer concentration among the 200 disclosed brokers/3PLs, and a direct comparison against Nuvocargo's scale and funding.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Addressable U.S.-Mexico cross-border truckload freight volume reachable via a vetted digital marketplace | 8,000,000 loads/year | $2,500 avg load value | $20.00bn GMV | HCP assumption: brokers/3PLs/forwarders segment reachable by a trust-vetted digital marketplace |
| Marketplace monetization rate | | 2.0% | $400m | HCP assumption: blended brokerage-fee-equivalent monetization across matched loads |
| **TAM** | | | **$400m** | Annual net marketplace-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration |  |  | **21.0%** | About 2.2 million loads facilitated annually by 2032 |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** |  |  | **$84m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Loads facilitated (thousands) | 100 | 250 | 500 | 850 | 1,250 | 1,700 | 2,200 |
| Net revenue per load | $26 | $28 | $30 | $32 | $34 | $36 | $38 |
| **Revenue** | **$3** | **$7** | **$15** | **$27** | **$43** | **$61** | **$84** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Business model / user | Workflow capability | Delivery | Hardest-to-copy advantage | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Cargado** | Marketplace/take-rate; brokers, 3PLs, forwarders, cross-border carriers | X vetted invite-only load board, X carrier vetting | Cloud marketplace | Personally vetted cross-border carrier network (650+ at Series A) | Undisclosed | $12m Series A; total and valuation undisclosed; LGVP, Conversion Capital, Assembly Ventures, Primary Venture Partners |
| Nuvocargo | Digital freight forwarder/marketplace; U.S.-Mexico shippers and carriers | X cross-border brokerage and marketplace; Partial invite-only vetting model vs. Cargado | Cloud platform plus brokerage operations | Broader freight-forwarding and customs-adjacent service scope | Undisclosed | Private; total funding not comparable here, materially larger than Cargado's disclosed total |
| DAT Freight & Analytics | Load board and market-rate data; brokers/carriers, primarily domestic U.S. | Partial cross-border coverage; No evidence of Cargado's carrier-vetting-first model | Cloud platform | Long-standing load-board network and rate-data history | Subscription | Private; capital data not comparable |
| Uber Freight | Digital freight brokerage/marketplace; shippers and carriers | X domestic and some cross-border brokerage; Partial invite-only vetting depth vs. Cargado | Cloud platform | Large capital base and shipper relationships | Undisclosed | Private (spun out of Uber); capital data not comparable |
| J.B. Hunt 360 | Digital freight marketplace; shippers and carriers, primarily domestic | X domestic marketplace; No evidence of cross-border-specific vetting workflow | Cloud platform | Large asset-based carrier network as backstop | Undisclosed | Public company product |
| Traditional cross-border customs brokers/forwarders | Manual brokerage services; shippers | Partial matching via phone/email/personal relationships; No evidence of a digital vetted marketplace | Manual/phone/email | Existing customs and carrier relationships | Commission-based | N/A |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [C.H. Robinson](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/chrw/statistics/) | 1.61x | Diversified freight brokerage, illustrates end-market multiple ceiling |
| [Landstar System](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/lstr/statistics/) | 1.44x | Asset-light freight network operator |
| [RXO](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/rxo/statistics/) | 0.96x | Pure-play asset-light freight brokerage spinoff |
| **Median** | **1.44x** | HCP uses 1.4x, at the median; freight brokerage and marketplace businesses structurally trade at low public multiples regardless of growth rate, and HCP does not assume Cargado escapes that ceiling without diligence evidence of a higher-margin monetization mix |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $45m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 4.44% |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 2.89% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $84m / 1.4x |
| Exit enterprise value | $117.6m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $3.4m / **1.7x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.7x / 4.4x |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Structurally low exit multiples:** every public comp in the freight-brokerage/marketplace category trades below 2.0x EV/LTM revenue, capping upside even in a strong operating scenario. HCP's base MOIC (1.7x) does not clear a typical venture return bar; this is a Watch, not a Pursue, until Cargado demonstrates a higher-margin monetization mix (factoring, insurance, customs) that could support a better comp set.
- **Direct, better-funded competition:** Nuvocargo targets the same U.S.-Mexico corridor with a broader service scope and a larger disclosed capital base. Require a direct win/loss and pricing comparison against Nuvocargo in diligence.
- **Carrier-vetting quality at scale:** the trust model that differentiates Cargado today (personal vetting of every carrier) may not scale linearly with network growth without either slowing growth or degrading vetting quality. Track vetting headcount and process automation as the carrier base grows.
- **Downside includes capital loss:** at 60% of base revenue and a floor multiple, HCP's downside case falls below 1.0x MOIC. This is a real, not merely theoretical, risk given the category's low structural multiples — size any eventual investment accordingly and revisit only if unit economics or monetization mix improve materially.

## 81. Beli

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://beliapp.com/) | [Founding story](https://beliapp.com/ourstory) | [Independent profile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beli_(app))

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Judy Thelen | Co-founder and CEO | Wikipedia and the company's own site identify Thelen, a Harvard Business School alumna, as co-founder; the concept originated from a shared Google Map of restaurants she built with Frost. |
| Eliot Frost | Co-founder | Co-built the original restaurant-tracking concept with Thelen; "Beli" is derived from Frost's high school nickname, per Wikipedia. |

### Product description

Beli is a restaurant-focused social app built around a comparative, Elo-style ranking system rather than absolute star ratings. After a visit, a user searches for the restaurant and is shown a short series of head-to-head comparisons against places they've already rated; a few taps place the new restaurant into the user's personal, continuously re-sorted list. Because ranking is relative to a user's own visited-restaurant history and social graph rather than an anonymous aggregate score, recommendations can be more personalized than Yelp- or Google-style review averages. The app also supports saved lists, photo tracking, and algorithmic recommendations based on taste similarity to friends and to other users with overlapping preferences. As of September 2025 the company reported over 75 million total reviews across 30,000 cities globally, with roughly 80% of users under 35.

### Thesis: why invest

Beli's own site and Wikipedia describe a $5.3m Series A led by Goodwater Capital that closed in November 2023, with total disclosed capital reaching $12m as of June 2025, including investment from FirstMark Capital. HCP notes that funding aggregators show a range of figures for the same events (a $6.15m total appears in one Crunchbase-derived summary), and could not locate a primary financing press release; the exact round size and structure should be confirmed directly with the company before any commitment.

Beli's asset is a genuine, multi-year-accumulated taste graph: 75 million-plus comparative rankings is a meaningfully large, hard-to-replicate dataset about what people actually prefer, not just what they rated. That dataset should, in principle, power both better consumer recommendations and a B2B restaurant-insights/advertising product, but Beli has disclosed no monetization publicly as of this writing — the entire revenue model in this memo is an HCP construction, not a company claim.

**What must be true:** Beli must convert engagement into a monetization product (subscription and/or restaurant advertising/insights) without degrading the trust that makes its rankings useful; growth must extend meaningfully beyond the New York/Chicago/San Francisco markets where it is concentrated; and the taste-graph advantage must remain defensible as Google, Yelp, and TikTok all add more personalized, algorithmic food-discovery features.

**Next-round milestones:** first disclosed monetization product (consumer subscription and/or restaurant-side revenue) live and generating measurable revenue, daily-active-user disclosure (currently withheld by the founders), evidence of engagement outside the three core launch cities, and a clean, single-source-confirmed financing history.

### Founder bet

Thelen and Frost built Beli from a personal tool (a shared Google Map) into an app with tens of millions of logged rankings, which is a credible signal of genuine product-market fit in a notoriously fickle consumer category. The founders' decision to withhold DAU figures publicly, even while touting cumulative review counts, is worth probing directly — it may reflect a deliberate go-to-market choice or may reflect softer engagement than the headline numbers suggest.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Engaged US dining-app users, premium tier | 20m | $50 | $1.00bn | HCP assumption: subscription-willing subset of Beli's addressable user base |
| Casual dining-app users, ad-supported value | 40m | $15 | $0.60bn | HCP assumption |
| Restaurant partner insights/advertising | 300,000 | $2,000 | $0.60bn | HCP assumption: B2B product entirely unconfirmed publicly |
| **TAM** | | | **$2.20bn** | Annual revenue pool across consumer and B2B monetization |
| HCP penetration | | | **5.9% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$130m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **5** | **12** | **25** | **48** | **75** | **105** | **130** |

Beli has disclosed no revenue publicly as of this writing; every figure in this table is an HCP assumption built to test the check, not a company projection.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Beli** | Comparative restaurant ranking and social discovery | X ranking, tracking, recommendations; No evidence monetization live | Mobile app | Multi-year comparative taste graph (75m+ rankings) | Undisclosed | $5.3m Series A (per company/Wikipedia); total $12m disclosed by June 2025; Goodwater Capital, FirstMark Capital |
| Yelp | Star-rating restaurant reviews and local search | X reviews and search; Partial personalization | Web/app | Enormous legacy review volume and local-business relationships | Ads/subscription (business side) | Public |
| Google Maps / Search | Restaurant discovery via reviews and local search | X reviews and discovery; Partial comparative ranking | Native mobile/web | Default distribution and location data | Ads | Alphabet product |
| OpenTable | Restaurant reservations plus reviews | Partial discovery; X reservations | Web/app | Reservation-system installed base with restaurants | Restaurant-side subscription/booking fees | Booking Holdings product |
| TikTok (food content) | Algorithmic short-video food discovery | Partial discovery via creator content; No evidence structured ranking | Native app | Massive algorithmic distribution | Ads | ByteDance product |

### Public comps and exit model

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Zero disclosed monetization:** the entire revenue build is an HCP construction. Require the company to share any monetization roadmap or test data before finalizing terms.
- **Financing-record ambiguity:** conflicting totals across sources for a company this well known suggest either informal disclosure practices or an unannounced additional close. Get a clean cap table.
- **Geographic concentration:** engagement appears concentrated in a handful of major US metros. Confirm usage distribution and international traction.
- **Incumbent response:** Yelp, Google, and TikTok can all add comparative-ranking or taste-graph features. Beli's defense is the multi-year data lead, which is real but not unlimited.

## 82. Brisk Teaching

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.briskteaching.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/brisk-teaching-raises-15-million-to-reinvent-classroom-technology-for-the-ai-era-302412034.html) | [Investor perspective](https://www.bvp.com/news/giving-teachers-their-time-back-our-investment-in-brisk-teaching)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Arman Jaffer | Founder and CEO | Previously worked in the White House Office of the Chief Technology Officer, on Google's mobile search team, and as a product manager on the Chan Zuckerberg Initiative's Education team (launched Notebooks); Forbes 30 Under 30 Education honoree; UC Berkeley CS/Economics graduate. |

### Product description

Brisk Teaching is a browser-native AI copilot for K-12 educators, layering into whatever tools a teacher already uses (Google Docs, Slides, Canvas, and similar) rather than requiring a separate destination app. It generates lesson plans, differentiates reading levels, drafts feedback and report-card comments, creates pop quizzes and activities, and — per its "Brisk Boost" feature — generates AI-powered student-facing activities. The pitch is time savings embedded directly in existing teacher workflows rather than another platform to log into. Brisk reports usage by more than 1 million educators across over 100 countries and more than 2,000 school partnerships, with five-fold user growth since its September 2024 seed round.

### Thesis: why invest

Brisk raised a $15m Series A in March 2025 led by Bessemer Venture Partners, with participation from prior investors Owl Ventures, South Park Commons, and Springbank Collective, on top of a $5m seed in September 2024 — $20m total disclosed funding. Brisk and SchoolAI announced their Series A and (in SchoolAI's case) similarly sized rounds within days of each other in spring 2025, reflecting how contested the "teacher AI copilot" category had become by that point.

Brisk's browser-extension distribution model is a genuinely different go-to-market bet than SchoolAI's platform model: it embeds into a teacher's existing tools rather than asking them to adopt a new one, which likely explains the reported five-fold user growth off a comparatively modest seed round. Whether that lighter-weight distribution model converts into district-level paid contracts as reliably as a full platform play is the open question, and — like SchoolAI — the education-software public comp set caps the modeled return unless Brisk earns a premium multiple through demonstrated retention.

**What must be true:** browser-extension distribution must convert into durable district-level paid contracts, not just free individual-teacher adoption; the product must maintain differentiation as Google and Microsoft add native AI features to the exact documents Brisk operates inside of; and per-teacher usage must translate into a monetizable unit, whether through district licensing or individual upgrades.

**Next-round milestones:** $20m ARR, 500 paying district or school contracts, net revenue retention above 110%, and clear evidence that free-to-paid conversion holds at scale rather than being concentrated in early-adopter districts.

### Founder bet

Jaffer's background spans policy (White House OCTO), a major consumer platform (Google), and an education-specific product launch at scale (CZI's Notebooks) — a relevant, if not deeply operator-heavy, combination for navigating both K-12 procurement and product design. As with SchoolAI, this is a single named founder at meaningful company scale; diligence should assess bench strength on the executive team.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| U.S. K-12 teachers (per-teacher paid tier) | 3,800,000 | $150 | $0.57bn | HCP assumption |
| International teachers in target markets | 4,000,000 | $80 | $0.32bn | HCP assumption |
| U.S. districts (district-wide contract) | 13,000 | $8,000 | $0.10bn | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$0.99bn** | Annual subscription-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **15.1% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$150m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Base case | 10 | 24 | 45 | 72 | 105 | 130 | 150 |
| Illustrative paying school/district contracts (cumulative) | 300 | 650 | 1,100 | 1,700 | 2,400 | 3,000 | 3,600 |

Brisk does not disclose pricing publicly (the company's pricing page was unreachable at the time of this memo); the per-teacher and per-district assumptions above are HCP estimates, not company-quoted figures.

### Competitive landscape

| SchoolAI | K-12 classroom AI platform | X teacher and student tools, full platform | Web platform | Batch peer; see SchoolAI memo | See SchoolAI memo | See SchoolAI memo |

| Khanmigo (Khan Academy) | AI tutor and teacher assistant | X student tutoring; X teacher tools | Web app | Khan Academy brand and content library | Subscription/district licensing | Nonprofit-affiliated; not a comparable capital structure |
| Google Gemini for Education | Bundled AI for schools | Partial teacher and student AI features | Native Workspace for Education | Default distribution to existing districts | Bundled/licensed | Alphabet product |
| Microsoft Copilot for Education | Bundled AI for schools | Partial teacher and student AI features | Native Microsoft 365 Education | Default distribution to existing districts | Bundled/licensed | Microsoft product |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Stride](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/lrn/statistics/) | 1.32x | K-12-adjacent online/managed education |

|---|---:|

| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $150m / 1.3x |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price versus comp set:** like SchoolAI, the modeled return is unattractive at the assumed $80m post-money unless Brisk earns a premium multiple through demonstrated retention. Negotiate price or structure before committing.
- **Free-to-paid conversion undisclosed:** 1 million educators using the product is a strong top-of-funnel number, but the company discloses no ARR or paying-account count. This is the single most important number to obtain in diligence.
- **Bundling risk:** because Brisk embeds directly into Google Docs, Slides, and Canvas, it is maximally exposed to those platforms adding native AI features that replicate its exact value proposition.
- **Why invest anyway:** the embedded, browser-native distribution model is a genuinely different and potentially more capital-efficient go-to-market than SchoolAI's platform approach, and five-fold growth off a small seed round is a real signal. This is a business worth funding at a disciplined price, not at an assumed premium valuation.

## 83. Doss

**Stage:** Series B (stage exception — see note below)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.doss.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.doss.com/news/announcing-our-18m-series-a) | [Series B announcement](https://www.doss.com/news/doss-raises-55m-series-b) | [TechCrunch Series B coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2026/03/24/doss-raises-55m-for-ai-inventory-management-that-plugs-into-erp/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Wiley Jones | Co-founder | Co-authored the company's Series A announcement; described prior ERP-systems experience before founding Doss. |
| Arnav | Co-founder | Co-founder per the same Series A announcement; full surname and background undisclosed in public sources. Confirm in diligence. |

### Product description

Doss (branded DossARP, the Adaptive Resource Platform) is an AI-native ERP and operations cloud built for mid-market physical-goods companies — primarily consumer brands in retail, wholesale, and manufacturing with roughly $20m-$250m in revenue, per Madrona's investment writeup. It unifies inventory management, order processing, accounting, and production into a single system built from composable, loosely connected databases, cloud services, and workflows designed to be reconfigured by both humans and AI agents. The company claims implementation in as little as two days versus the years incumbent ERP systems can require, directly targeting the well-documented high failure rate of traditional ERP rollouts.

### Thesis: why invest

**Stage exception:** the roster flagged Doss as a Seed/Series A target. It has since raised an $18m Series A led by Theory Ventures (April 2025) and a $55m Series B co-led by Madrona and Premji Invest (March 2026), bringing total disclosed funding to $73m at a disclosed $250m post-money valuation. Per this batch's mandate, HCP retains Doss with this exception explained, and prices the return model directly off the disclosed $250m post-money.

Doss's differentiated angle within the AI-native ERP wave is a narrower, more defensible ICP than horizontal challengers: mid-market physical-goods companies with inventory, production, and multi-entity complexity that outgrow spreadsheets and QuickBooks but are poorly served by NetSuite's implementation cost and timeline. Disclosed customer examples (a peanut-butter manufacturer, a construction/glass-fabrication company, a private-equity firm deploying Doss across its portfolio) support a genuine mid-market physical-operations wedge, distinct from Campfire's software-company-weighted customer base in this batch.

**What must be true:** the two-day implementation claim must hold at scale as customer complexity grows (multi-location, multi-currency, more complex bills of materials); Doss must retain and expand within its physical-goods niche rather than needing to broaden into software companies where Campfire and Rillet already compete; and revenue growth must justify the rapid Series A-to-Series-B valuation step-up (roughly $75m implied post-Series-A to $250m post-Series-B in under a year).

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed ARR at the next financing event, evidence of successful multi-location/multi-entity deployments, gross margin sustained above 70%, and expansion revenue from the initial customer cohort.

### Founder bet

Wiley Jones and a co-founder identified only as "Arnav" in public sources both bring direct prior ERP-systems experience, per the company's own Series A announcement, which is a credible domain-fit signal for a product explicitly targeting ERP-implementation failure. The rapid Series A-to-Series-B progression (April 2025 to March 2026, an eleven-month gap) with a new lead investor (Madrona, joined by Premji Invest) at each stage suggests external validation of execution, though as with Campfire, HCP should confirm whether governance and key-person structures have kept pace with the fundraising velocity.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Accounts | Annual contract | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Mid-market physical-goods companies ($20m-$250m revenue) | 25,000 | $40,000 | $1.00bn | HCP assumption |
| Larger multi-location physical-goods operators | 4,000 | $150,000 | $600m | HCP assumption |
| Enterprise / PE-portfolio deployments | 500 | $500,000 | $250m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | 29,500 | | **$1.85bn** | Annual adaptive-ERP software pool for physical-goods operators |
| HCP penetration | | | **8.7%** | ~1,850 blended accounts by 2032 |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$161m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|

| Blended ACV | $50k | $58k | $65k | $72k | $78k | $83k | $87k |
| **Revenue** | **$6** | **$15** | **$31** | **$58** | **$90** | **$124** | **$161** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow coverage | Delivery | Hardest-to-copy advantage | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Doss** | Adaptive ERP/operations; mid-market physical-goods companies | X inventory, orders, accounting, production | Cloud SaaS, composable architecture | Fast implementation plus agent-reconfigurable architecture for physical-goods complexity | Undisclosed | $73m total; $250m disclosed post-money; Theory Ventures, Madrona, Premji Invest |

| Fishbowl | SMB inventory management | X inventory management; No evidence AI-native reconfiguration | On-premise/cloud hybrid | Long-tenured SMB inventory installed base | Custom | Private; valuation not used |
| Brightpearl | Retail/wholesale operations platform | X order/inventory/accounting for retail; Partial manufacturing depth | Cloud SaaS | Retail-specific workflow depth | Custom | Sage product (acquired; public parent) |

### Public comps and exit model

The selected ERP comp set is reused from the reference file's Tailor memo (same tickers, same July 18, 2026 snapshot): [Oracle](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/orcl/statistics/) 7.42x, [SAP](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/sap/statistics/) 4.24x, [Workday](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/wday/statistics/) 3.57x, [Manhattan Associates](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/manh/statistics/) 8.62x, and [Shopify](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/shop/statistics/) 12.49x. Median EV/LTM revenue is **7.42x**; HCP uses 3.5x, below median and below Campfire's selected multiple given Doss's narrower niche and less-diversified customer base disclosed to date.

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money / ownership | $250m disclosed / 0.80% |
| Future dilution / exit ownership | 35% / 0.52% |
| 2032 revenue / multiple / EV | $161m / 3.5x / $563.5m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $2.93m / **1.5x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.6x / 2.8x |

Downside: revenue $96.6m (60%), multiple 2.5x → EV $241.5m → proceeds $1.26m → 0.6x. Upside: revenue $241.5m (150%), multiple 4.5x → EV $1.09bn → proceeds $5.65m → 2.8x.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price outstrips modeled return:** at a disclosed $250m post-money, even a healthy bottom-up revenue build produces a sub-2x base MOIC for a $1.0m-$2.5m check. This is the weakest base-case return in the batch; only pursue with a lower effective price or a larger allocation that changes the diligence calculus.
- **Narrow niche ceiling:** the physical-goods mid-market ICP is real but smaller than the software-company TAM Campfire and Rillet target. Confirm whether Doss's roadmap extends beyond this niche or whether it will remain a smaller, more durable business.
- **Rapid valuation step-up:** roughly a 3x post-money increase in eleven months (implied ~$75m to $250m) requires very strong underlying growth to justify at the next round; a disappointing Series C could compress returns further for later entrants.
- **Why invest anyway:** the founding team's direct ERP-systems background, tier-1 new investor validation at each round (Theory, then Madrona/Premji), and a genuinely differentiated fast-implementation product for an underserved physical-goods niche are real positives. This belongs on a watchlist for a better-priced entry point (secondary, extension round, or renegotiated allocation) rather than an outright pass.

## 84. Spellbook

**Stage:** Series B (verified; roster hint said Series A). Spellbook priced a $20m Series A (Jan. 2024, after an earlier $10.9m round) and a $50m Series B at a disclosed $350m post-money on October 9, 2025; HCP keeps Spellbook in scope per the batch's Series-B exception, using the disclosed price directly.
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://spellbook.com/) | [Series B financing](https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20251009110230/en/Spellbook-Raises-$50M-Series-B-to-Expand-AI-Contract-Review-Platform) | [Coverage with valuation detail](https://siliconangle.com/2025/10/09/legal-ai-firm-spellbook-raises-50m-expand-contract-review-platform/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Scott Stevenson | Co-founder and CEO | Identified as co-founder and CEO in SiliconANGLE's Series B coverage; quoted describing Spellbook's positioning as "the spreadsheet moment for lawyers." |
| Additional co-founders | Undisclosed | Spellbook's parent entity is legally named "Rally" per Crunchbase records; no additional co-founders are named in the sources reviewed. Confirm full founding-team composition in diligence. |

### Product description

Spellbook is an AI copilot for transactional lawyers, positioned by its CEO as "Cursor for contracts." Built on OpenAI's GPT-5 and other large language models and integrated directly into Microsoft Word, it offers contract review and redlining, drafting from scratch or saved templates, benchmarking against industry-standard clauses, natural-language Q&A on legal documents, firm-specific "Playbooks" that encode internal standards, and an agentic "Associate" feature for multi-document workflow management. A newer "Autonomous Contract Management" (ACM) offering extends toward end-to-end contract lifecycle management. The company reports more than 10 million contracts reviewed and 4,500+ legal teams across 80+ countries, with named customers including Dropbox, Nestlé, eBay, Kennedys, Asics, Crocs, Wealthsimple, Franklin Templeton, and Panasonic.

### Thesis: why invest

Spellbook raised a $10.9m round in May 2023 led by Moxxie Ventures, a $20m Series A in January 2024 led by Inovia Capital, and a $50m Series B on October 9, 2025 at a disclosed $350m post-money valuation, led by Keith Rabois at Khosla Ventures with Threshold Ventures newly joining alongside returning investors Inovia, Bling Capital, Moxxie, and Path Ventures. Total disclosed funding exceeds $80m. In March 2026 the company added a $40m debt facility from RBCx earmarked for acquisitions, signaling an intent to consolidate the legal-AI category rather than only build organically. The 4,500-legal-team, 10-million-contract, 80-country footprint is a genuinely large disclosed install base for a company at this stage.

The moat is workflow depth inside Microsoft Word plus accumulated playbook and clause-benchmarking data: once a firm has encoded its standards into Spellbook's Playbooks and trained associates on the Review/Draft/Compare/Ask workflow, switching to a competitor means rebuilding that institutional knowledge. The RBCx acquisition facility suggests management intends to buy that same kind of embedded position in adjacent legal workflows rather than build every feature from scratch.

**What must be true:** the large user-team count must convert into expanding, high-value seats rather than remaining concentrated in low-tier or trial usage; the ACM push into full contract-lifecycle management must succeed against dedicated CLM incumbents; and planned acquisitions (funded by the RBCx facility) must integrate cleanly rather than fragmenting the product.

**Next-round milestones:** $60m+ ARR, net revenue retention above 120%, at least one successful, integrated acquisition under the ACM strategy, and expansion of the AmLaw-200 and Fortune 500 in-house customer base beyond current named logos.

### Founder bet

Stevenson's public framing — legal work as being at its "spreadsheet moment" — reflects a clear, simply stated thesis about AI's role in transactional law, and the company has executed on it with real scale (10M+ contracts, 4,500+ teams) ahead of a $350m priced round from a top-tier lead investor. The founding team beyond Stevenson is not established in sources reviewed; HCP should confirm the full team and its division of technical and commercial responsibility before finalizing diligence.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| AmLaw 200 and other large firms | 300 | $150,000 | $45m | HCP assumption: firm-wide deployment |
| Mid-size law firms | 10,000 | $20,000 | $200m | HCP assumption |
| In-house legal departments | 15,000 | $25,000 | $375m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | 25,300 | | **$620m** | Annual legal-drafting AI software pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **33.9% of TAM revenue** | Consistent with a large existing 4,500-team base continuing to expand in seat depth |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$210m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Revenue | 16 | 30 | 50 | 78 | 115 | 155 | 210 |
| Illustrative legal teams (paid) | 4,500 | 6,500 | 9,000 | 12,000 | 15,500 | 19,000 | 22,500 |

2026 team count (4,500) is the company-disclosed current figure; note this includes a broad mix of firm sizes and tiers, so blended revenue per team is modest and rises only gradually as HCP assumes deeper seat penetration within existing accounts.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Spellbook** | AI contract drafting and review | X review, draft, compare, ask, playbooks; Partial full contract-lifecycle management (ACM, in development) | Microsoft Word add-in plus cloud | Word-native workflow depth plus firm-specific playbook data | Undisclosed; 7-day free trial | $50m Series B at $350m valuation; $80m+ total; Khosla Ventures, Inovia, Threshold |
| Ironclad | Contract lifecycle management | X full CLM workflow; Partial AI drafting | Cloud | Deep CLM installed base | Enterprise custom | Private; valuation not used |
| Robin AI | AI contract review and drafting | X review and drafting; Partial full CLM | Cloud plus Word integration | Enterprise legal-team focus | Custom | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Harvey | AI legal assistant for law firms | X broad legal research and drafting; Partial contract-specific playbooks | Cloud/API | Large-firm AmLaw penetration and funding scale | Enterprise custom | Private; valuation not used |
| LinkSquares | Contract management and analytics | X CLM and analytics; Partial AI drafting | Cloud | In-house legal department focus | Custom | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| DocuSign (Insight/CLM) | E-signature plus contract lifecycle | X signature and CLM; Partial AI review | Cloud | Massive e-signature distribution | Bundled/custom | Public |
| Thomson Reuters (CoCounsel) | Legal AI research and drafting (incl. former Casetext) | X research and drafting; Partial transactional playbooks | Cloud, bundled into Reuters legal suite | Legal-content and research incumbency | Bundled/custom | Public |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Thomson Reuters](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/tri/statistics/) | 5.76x | Legal content, research, and AI incumbent |
| [Intapp](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/inta/statistics/) | 3.78x | Professional-services (incl. legal) workflow software |
| [DocuSign](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/docu/statistics/) | 2.87x | Contract and agreement workflow software |

| **Median** | **3.33x** | HCP uses 3.5x, roughly in line with median given Spellbook's scale lead |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $350m, disclosed October 2025 |
| Initial ownership | 0.57% |
| Cumulative future dilution | 30%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 0.40% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $210m / 3.5x |
| Exit enterprise value | $735m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $2.94m / **1.47x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.63x / 2.84x |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price:** at a disclosed $350m post-money, a $2.0m check buys well under 1% ownership, and even a strong outcome yields a modest MOIC. Only pursue with a smaller check or a secondary/structured entry at a discount.
- **Category crowding at the top:** Harvey and Thomson Reuters CoCounsel both have significant scale and funding; Spellbook's differentiation is Word-native workflow and playbook depth, which incumbents could erode over time.
- **Acquisition-integration risk:** the RBCx debt facility signals an acquisitive strategy; poorly integrated acquisitions could dilute product coherence and burn cash without adding durable ARR.
- **Thin founding-team disclosure:** only one founder (Stevenson) is named in sources reviewed. Confirm full team, equity, and governance structure in diligence.

## 85. Pickle

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Diligence
**Links:** [Company](https://www.shoponpickle.com/) | [Series A report](https://alleywatch.com/2025/04/pickle-peer-to-peer-clothing-rental-marketplace-brian-mcmahon/) | [Seed report](https://techcrunch.com/2023/10/11/peer-to-peer-fashion-rental-marketplace-pickle-picks-up-8-million/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Brian McMahon | Co-founder and CEO | AlleyWatch identifies McMahon, a former Blackstone analyst, as CEO and co-founder. |
| Julia O'Mara | Co-founder | AlleyWatch identifies O'Mara, also a former Blackstone analyst, as co-founder; the pair previously worked together at Blackstone. |

### Product description

Pickle is a peer-to-peer fashion rental marketplace — described by investors and press as "the Airbnb of fashion." Unlike Rent the Runway's owned-inventory model, Pickle does not buy, warehouse, or manage clothing itself; supply comes directly from individual lenders' closets, and renters browse and book items the same way they would on a traditional rental platform. As of the April 2025 Series A report, the platform listed more than 200,000 items from over 2,000 brands, with tens of thousands of renters and lenders active across the U.S., and rental prices typically 80–90% below retail. The company charges a service fee on each transaction plus, in select markets, a same-day courier delivery fee.

### Thesis: why invest

Pickle raised a $12m Series A in April 2025, co-led by FirstMark Capital and Craft Ventures with participation from Burst Capital (led by former Yelp executives) and FJ Labs, following an $8m seed round in October 2023 (also led by Craft Ventures and FirstMark). Total disclosed capital is $20m. AlleyWatch reports 4x net revenue growth and 3x monthly-active-user growth over the trailing year, with nearly half of monthly active users also being weekly active users — an unusually strong engagement signal for a rental marketplace, where usage is inherently occasional rather than daily.

The asset-light, peer-to-peer supply model is the core structural advantage over owned-inventory competitors: no warehousing, no depreciation risk, and a catalog that can scale with lender participation rather than capital raised. The risk of this model is quality and reliability control across thousands of individual lenders, which Pickle must solve operationally rather than through inventory ownership.

**What must be true:** lender supply quality and reliability must remain consistent as the network scales past a few thousand active lenders; logistics (shipping, cleaning/care standards between renters) must stay economical without Pickle owning the inventory; and repeat-rental behavior must continue at the reported near-50%-weekly-active rate as the user base grows beyond early adopters.

**Next-round milestones:** 500,000+ listed items, disclosed gross margin after logistics and lender payouts, evidence of repeat-lender and repeat-renter cohorts at scale, and expansion beyond the current core U.S. markets.

### Founder bet

McMahon and O'Mara's Blackstone analyst background is a reasonable signal of financial and operational rigor, and the AlleyWatch profile notes the founders pivoted toward the current peer-to-peer model after observing organic user behavior (people recommending items from their own closets) — a good sign of listening to the market rather than forcing a thesis. Diligence should probe how much of the reported growth is organic versus paid, and how lender retention compares to renter retention.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Active P2P fashion renters (US, occasion-driven) | 15m | $25 | $375m | HCP assumption: net platform take across average annual rental frequency |
| Lender-side monetization (listing/boost fees) | 800,000 | $60 | $48m | HCP assumption |
| Brand/wholesale rental partnerships | — | — | $50m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$473m** | Annual net-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **19.0% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$90m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **5** | **12** | **23** | **38** | **57** | **72** | **90** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Pickle** | Peer-to-peer fashion rental marketplace | X listing, booking, payments; X peer-to-peer logistics | Mobile/web marketplace, courier delivery in select markets | Asset-light P2P supply and high engagement (near-50% weekly-active share) | Per-transaction service fee | $12m Series A; $20m total; valuation undisclosed; FirstMark, Craft Ventures, Burst Capital, FJ Labs |
| Rent the Runway | Owned-inventory clothing rental | X rental and styling; No evidence P2P supply | Owned warehouses, shipping | Brand relationships and curated owned inventory | Subscription and à la carte | Public |
| Poshmark | Peer-to-peer resale (not rental) marketplace | X resale listing/selling; No evidence rental | Mobile/web marketplace | Large resale community and social-selling features | Seller commission | Private (acquired by Naver); capital data not comparable |
| ThredUp | Resale marketplace with owned processing | X resale intake/resale; No evidence rental | Owned processing facilities, shipping | Large-scale garment processing infrastructure | Consignment/commission | Public |
| By Rotation | Peer-to-peer fashion rental marketplace (UK-based) | X P2P rental listing and booking | Mobile/web marketplace | Early mover in UK P2P rental | Per-transaction commission | Private; capital data undisclosed here |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Etsy](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/etsy/statistics/) | 3.32x | Curated peer-to-peer marketplace comp |
| [ThredUp](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/tdup/statistics/) | 2.66x | Apparel resale/recommerce comp |
| [The RealReal](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/real/statistics/) | 2.34x | Authenticated apparel resale comp |
| **Median** | **2.66x** | HCP uses 1.5x, a 44% discount reflecting rental-specific logistics and quality-control costs not borne by pure resale comps |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $60m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 3.33% ($2.0m / $60m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 2.167% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $90m / 1.5x |
| Exit enterprise value | $135m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $2.925m / **1.46x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.585x / 3.66x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($54m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (1.5x − 1 turn = 0.5x, floored to 1.0x) yields $54m EV, $1.17m proceeds, 0.585x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($135m) at 2.5x yields $337.5m EV, $7.313m proceeds, 3.66x MOIC.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Quality and reliability control:** peer-to-peer supply means item condition and lender reliability are harder to guarantee than owned inventory. Require data on dispute/refund rates and lender rating distributions.
- **Logistics cost creep:** courier delivery in select markets could erode the asset-light cost advantage if expanded broadly. Track delivery cost per transaction over time.
- **Seasonality:** occasion-driven rental demand (weddings, galas, holidays) is inherently lumpy. Assess revenue seasonality and off-peak retention.
- **Competitive convergence:** Poshmark, ThredUp, and RealReal all have large existing user bases that could add rental features. Pickle's edge is P2P-native supply, not brand or scale, which is replicable if a larger player commits to it.

## 86. Ansa

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://ansa.dev/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/ansa-raises-14-million-series-a-funding-to-redefine-merchant-transaction-solutions-302131675.html) | [TechCrunch coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2024/04/30/wallet-as-a-service-startup-ansa-raises-14m-with-female-investors-leading-the-way/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Sophia Goldberg | Co-founder and CEO | TechCrunch reports she was previously a product manager at Adyen; quoted in the company's blog on building "stored value wallet as a service." |
| JT Cho | Co-founder | TechCrunch reports prior software-engineering experience at Affirm. |

### Product description

Ansa is a white-labeled, "wallet-as-a-service" platform: it lets merchants and platforms launch a branded stored-value wallet (closed-loop balances, gift-card-style credits, loyalty-linked funds) without building the ledger, compliance, and payment-acceptance stack themselves. The pitch to merchants is that a stored-value wallet reduces card-network fees on repeat transactions and increases visit frequency by pre-loading customer funds. Ansa's own case study reports a 30% increase in visit frequency at Compass Coffee after launching a stored-value wallet. The company targets coffee and quick-service restaurant chains, marketplaces, and retail/convenience as initial verticals, with a self-serve incentive engine and merchant analytics portal layered on top of the core wallet infrastructure.

### Thesis: why invest

Stored value is a proven mechanic (Starbucks' app-loaded balance is the canonical example) but building it in-house requires a regulated money-transmission-adjacent ledger, reconciliation, and compliance stack that most mid-market merchants cannot justify. Ansa's April 2024 $14m Series A, led by Renegade Partners with Bain Capital Ventures, BoxGroup, Wischoff Ventures, and B37 Ventures participating (95.6% of the round from female investors, a notable signal TechCrunch highlighted), gives it roughly $20m in total funding to build this out. The company reports doubling its customer base year over year as of Q1 2024, though it has not disclosed absolute customer counts.

The moat, in principle, is switching cost once a merchant's loyalty and balance data lives inside Ansa's ledger. In practice, stored-value infrastructure is a thin-margin, highly competitive category with entrenched players (Fiserv, Marqeta-powered issuers, and numerous loyalty/gift-card vendors) and Ansa has not disclosed enough absolute scale for HCP to underwrite conviction that it is winning share meaningfully.

**What must be true:** stored-value programs must generate durable per-merchant revenue well above thin transaction-processing margins; Ansa must win larger platform/marketplace deals, not just small QSR locations, to reach real scale; and the company must show absolute (not just relative) growth numbers in its next disclosure.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed absolute customer/merchant counts in the hundreds with visible cohort retention, $8m-$12m annualized platform revenue, at least one marketplace-scale enterprise deployment, and gross margin data showing the wallet model clears standard payments-infrastructure economics.

### Founder bet

Goldberg (Adyen) and Cho (Affirm) both come from strong payments pedigrees, and the Series A syndicate quality (Bain Capital Ventures, Renegade Partners) is a real positive signal. The concern is not team quality but category economics: stored-value wallet infrastructure is structurally thin-margin, and Ansa has not yet disclosed the absolute scale evidence needed to show it can out-earn that structural ceiling.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---|---|
| SMB merchant locations (coffee, QSR, retail) | 50,000 | $6,000 | $300m | HCP assumption |
| Marketplace/platform enterprise deployments | 500 | $200,000 | $100m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$400m** | Annual wallet-infrastructure revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **27.0%** | ~1,800 wallet programs live by 2032 |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$108m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Wallet programs live | 50 | 150 | 350 | 650 | 1,000 | 1,400 | 1,800 |
| Avg. annual revenue/program | $10k | $14k | $20k | $28k | $38k | $48k | $60k |
| **Revenue** | **$1** | **$2** | **$7** | **$18** | **$38** | **$67** | **$108** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Ansa** | White-label stored-value wallet infra | X wallet issuance, incentives, merchant analytics | SDK/API | Balance-and-loyalty data lock-in per merchant | Undisclosed | $14m Series A; ~$20m total; valuation undisclosed; Renegade, Bain Capital Ventures, BoxGroup, Wischoff |
| Fiserv | Core banking/payments, includes stored value | X broad stored-value and card issuing; Partial merchant-branded self-serve tooling | Enterprise platform | Bank-distribution scale | Custom | Public |
| Marqeta | Card issuing infra (powers many wallets) | X issuing/wallet rails; Partial merchant-facing self-serve tooling | API | Issuing scale, bank partnerships | Usage-based | Public |
| PayPal (branded balance/wallet) | Consumer wallet at platform scale | X stored balance, payments; No evidence white-label merchant offering | App/API | Massive consumer distribution | Take rate | Public |
| Stored Value Solutions (Fiserv) | Gift card and stored-value programs | X gift-card/stored-value issuance | Enterprise platform | Legacy retail gift-card incumbency | Custom | Fiserv subsidiary |
| Bird (loyalty/stored-value tech) | Loyalty and stored-value for restaurants | X loyalty and stored-value; Partial broader platform use cases | SaaS/API | Restaurant-vertical focus | Custom | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Punchh (PAR Technology) | Restaurant loyalty and stored value | X loyalty/stored value for restaurant chains | SaaS | Restaurant enterprise incumbency | Custom | PAR Technology subsidiary; public parent |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Marqeta](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/mq/statistics/) | 1.76x | Card/wallet issuing infrastructure |
| [PayPal](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pypl/statistics/) | 1.55x | Consumer stored-balance wallet at scale |
| [Fiserv](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/fi/statistics/) | 2.63x | Core payments/stored-value infrastructure |
| **Median** | **1.76x** | HCP uses 1.4x, near the low end, reflecting thin-margin category economics and unproven absolute scale |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $70m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 2.86% |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 1.86% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $108m / 1.4x |
| Exit enterprise value | $151.2m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $2.81m / **1.40x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.60x / 3.61x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($64.8m) at 1.0x floor (1.4x minus one turn would be 0.4x, floored) = $64.8m EV, $1.20m proceeds, 0.60x — a capital-loss scenario. Upside detail: 150% of base revenue ($162m) at one turn more (2.4x) = $388.8m EV, $7.22m proceeds, 3.61x.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Structural thin margin:** stored-value infrastructure sits in a category with inherently modest take rates. Absent evidence Ansa earns meaningfully more per merchant than the model above, the base and downside cases do not clear a venture return threshold, which is why HCP recommends **Pass** at the assumed $70m entry price.
- **Undisclosed absolute scale:** "doubled customer base" without a base number is not underwritable. Any renewed interest should require disclosed absolute merchant counts and cohort retention.
- **Competitive crowding:** Fiserv, Marqeta-powered issuers, and vertical loyalty players (Punchh, Bird) all compete for the same merchant budget line.
- **Reconsideration path:** if Ansa discloses a large enterprise/marketplace deployment (not just SMB locations) with materially higher per-account revenue than modeled here, or if entry price is meaningfully below the $70m HCP assumption, this could move back to Diligence.

## 87. Partiful

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://partiful.com/) | [Series A report](https://fortune.com/2023/05/23/partiful-founders-startup-raises-series-a/) | [Additional coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2024/11/18/partiful-is-googles-best-app-of-2024/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Shreya Murthy | Co-founder and CEO | Fortune and multiple outlets identify Murthy as co-founder and CEO; she and Tao met while working at Palantir Technologies. |
| Joy Tao | Co-founder and CTO | Identified as co-founder and CTO across company and press sources. |

### Product description

Partiful is a mobile-first event invitation and RSVP platform built around SMS-native distribution: rather than routing invitations through email or Facebook Events, hosts share a link and guests text in their phone numbers to receive updates. The product is design-forward, with customizable invitation themes, group chat, RSVP tracking, and photo-sharing tools built around the arc of a single event. Partiful was named Google's "best app" of 2024 by TechCrunch's reporting on Google's year-end list, and the company has run limited brand partnerships (e.g., a Chipotle Cinco de Mayo promotion). Founded in 2020, Partiful has built one of the more culturally resonant consumer-social products of the last several years among Gen Z and millennial users, particularly for informal, in-person gatherings.

### Thesis: why invest

Partiful raised a $20m Series A led by Andreessen Horowitz (with Initialized Capital participating), reported in Fortune's May 2023 profile of the founders; PitchBook-derived estimates place the pre-money valuation near $120m (implying a post-money in the $140m range), though HCP could not confirm this directly from a primary source. In December 2024, unconfirmed press reports floated a possible Series B at a $400m valuation, which a company spokesperson disputed — HCP treats that figure as unverified and excludes it from the model.

Partiful's core asset is a genuinely large, highly engaged social graph built around real-world events, with strong organic virality and brand recognition (the Google "best app" distinction is real third-party validation of product quality and cultural relevance). The structural risk, and the reason this memo does not recommend pursuing at this price without more evidence, is that HCP found no public indication of a confirmed monetization model — no disclosed subscription tier, no disclosed take rate on paid events or ticketing, and no disclosed advertising or data product. A product this beloved is a strong foundation for a business, but it is not yet evidence of one.

**What must be true:** Partiful must convert its social graph into at least one confirmed revenue stream (premium features, brand/commerce partnerships, or ticketing) at a scale that justifies a valuation in the hundreds of millions; growth must not depend entirely on a single platform's algorithmic goodwill (SMS distribution and organic app-store discovery); and the product's Gen Z-coded brand must translate into paying behavior, not just usage.

**Next-round milestones:** first disclosed monetization product live and generating measurable revenue, confirmed current valuation (to resolve the denied $400m report), evidence of usage growth beyond the current core demographic, and disclosed retention/DAU metrics.

### Founder bet

Murthy and Tao met at Palantir and built a product that genuinely changed how a generation plans informal gatherings — Fortune's own framing (overcoming investor skepticism of "two young female founders" building a "party-planning startup") suggests real conviction and execution against early doubt. The founder bet here is strong; the business-model bet is the open question, and HCP's "Watch" recommendation reflects that specific gap rather than any doubt about the founders or the product's cultural traction.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| US and select-international annual event hosts | 55m | $8 | $440m | HCP assumption: premium-tools willingness to pay, entirely unconfirmed by any disclosed Partiful product |
| Brand/commerce partnerships | 6,000 deals | $50,000 | $300m | HCP assumption |
| Paid-event/ticketing take rate | $2.0bn paid-event volume | 3% | $60m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$800m** | Annual revenue pool across entirely hypothetical monetization products |
| HCP penetration | | | **22.5% of TAM revenue** | Aggressive, reflecting Partiful's outsized existing engagement; should be discounted further absent any monetization evidence |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$180m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **5** | **15** | **35** | **65** | **105** | **145** | **180** |

Partiful has disclosed no revenue publicly. This entire table is an HCP construction built to stress-test the check against a plausible, not confirmed, monetization path.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Partiful** | SMS-native event invitations and RSVP | X invitations, RSVP, group chat; No evidence monetization live | Mobile app, SMS distribution | Design-led virality and large social/event graph | Undisclosed | $20m Series A (reported); total and current valuation undisclosed; a16z, Initialized Capital |
| Evite | Digital invitation and RSVP platform | X invitations and RSVP; Partial modern design/virality | Web/app | Long-standing brand recognition | Freemium/subscription, ads | Private; capital data not comparable |
| Facebook Events | Event creation within the Facebook/Meta ecosystem | X invitations and RSVP; X native distribution | Native app within Meta platforms | Default distribution inside an existing massive social graph | Free (ad-supported platform) | Meta product |
| Luma | Event registration and ticketing for professional/community events | X registration and ticketing; Partial casual-gathering fit | Web/app | Professional/creator-community focus, integrated ticketing | Freemium plus ticketing fees | Private; capital data undisclosed here |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Reddit](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/rddt/statistics/) | 12.99x | High-growth, highly engaged consumer-social comp |
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | High-engagement consumer-discovery comp |
| [Snap](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/snap/statistics/) | 1.48x | Younger-skewing consumer-social comp |
| [Bumble](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/bmbl/statistics/) | 0.85x | Social-matching consumer comp |
| **Median** | **2.215x** | HCP uses 1.5x, below median given zero disclosed monetization |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $130m, HCP assumption (near the last confirmed 2023 valuation, since no subsequent round is confirmed) |
| Initial ownership | 1.923% ($2.5m reference check / $130m — see note below) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 1.25% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $180m / 1.5x |
| Exit enterprise value | $270m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $3.375m / **1.35x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.54x / 3.375x |

Note: ownership arithmetic is run on the model check of $2.5m for clean comparability with the reference conventions; the actual proposed HCP check for Partiful is $1.5m, sized down from the $2.5m ceiling specifically because of the unproven-monetization risk. MOIC is invariant to check size at a fixed post-money and dilution, so the ratio above applies at either check size — HCP simply proposes committing less capital at that ratio given the risk. Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($108m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (1.5x − 1 turn = 0.5x, floored to 1.0x) yields $108m EV, $1.35m proceeds, 0.54x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($270m) at 2.5x yields $675m EV, $8.4375m proceeds, 3.375x MOIC.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Unproven monetization:** the single largest risk in this file. Do not size up the check until Partiful discloses or tests a real revenue product.
- **Valuation uncertainty:** the denied $400m Series B report creates real ambiguity about current price. Confirm valuation directly before any term discussion.
- **Platform/distribution dependency:** SMS-native growth and app-store discovery are not fully within Partiful's control. Assess concentration risk in acquisition channels.
- **Why invest anyway:** genuine, durable cultural relevance (Google's 2024 "best app") and a founding team that has already proven it can build a product people love in a crowded category — if a monetization signal appears, this becomes a much stronger file quickly, which is why HCP recommends watching closely rather than passing outright.

## 88. Isembard

**Stage:** Series A (screened at Seed per roster)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://www.isembard.com/) | [Seed announcement](https://techcrunch.com/2025/04/24/british-startup-isembard-lands-9m-to-reshore-manufacturing-for-critical-industries/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.isembard.com/blogs-and-articles/isembard-raises-50m-series-a-to-open-25-ai-powered-factories-serving-aerospace-and-defence)

### Stage-progression note

Isembard was assigned to this batch as a Seed-stage company. It closed a £7m (~$9m) seed round in April 2025 and then a $50m Series A in March 2026 — under a year later — led by Union Square Ventures. Per the instruction that a Series B (or, here, an unusually fast, large Series A) may be retained with an explained exception, this memo models entry against the Series A, not the original seed terms.

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Alexander Fitzgerald | Founder and CEO | Studied biochemistry, worked as a UK government business-policy adviser, founded a broadband company later acquired by Octopus Telecom, and encountered manufacturing supply-chain inefficiencies firsthand while serving with a UK military reserve unit — the stated origin of Isembard. |

### Product description

Isembard is a software-first precision-manufacturing company aiming to reshore critical-parts production (aerospace, defense, energy) using a distributed network of smaller factories rather than one large facility. Each factory runs on the company's proprietary MasonOS software platform, which coordinates quoting, scheduling, machine operations, quality checks, and workflow, and the company operates both company-owned and franchised factories under a shared operating model. Its first factory began operating in London, and the company's stated plan is to open 25 factories by the end of 2026 across the UK, US, Germany, France, and Ukraine, with most of the near-term build-out concentrated in the US.

### Thesis: why invest

Isembard is targeting a real and well-documented structural problem: the company cites a $1.8 trillion annual component-manufacturing market where small, aging, owner-operated shops produce 95% of output, and many owners are approaching retirement without succession plans — a genuine capacity gap for defense, aerospace, and energy supply chains in the US, UK, and Europe. The company's seed-to-Series-A pace (roughly 11 months, $9m to $50m) is unusually fast and reflects strong investor conviction: Union Square Ventures led the Series A, with new investors Tamarack Global and IQ Capital (both deep-tech/defense-focused) and existing investors Notion Capital and CIV, alongside angels including Deel's CEO Alex Bouaziz, Dexory Robotics' CEO Andrei Danescu, and former Wise CFO Matt Briers.

The speed of this progression, however, is precisely why HCP must be careful about entry price. A distributed-factory model franchised at pace across five countries in under two years is operationally ambitious, and the fast up-round means a small check today buys in at a valuation that already prices in significant execution success that has not yet been demonstrated at the 25-factory scale the company is targeting.

**What must be true:** the franchise/distributed-factory model must maintain MasonOS-driven quality and delivery consistency across independently operated sites; the US expansion (the stated majority of near-term build-out) must proceed without the regulatory and defense-industrial-base friction that has slowed other reshoring efforts; and unit economics per factory must scale faster than the capital required to open each new site.

**Next-round milestones:** at least 15 of the planned 25 factories operational and generating revenue, disclosed per-factory revenue and margin data, at least one named large defense or aerospace prime as a customer, and evidence the franchise sites match company-operated site quality and delivery metrics.

### Founder bet

The bet is on a non-manufacturing-background founder (biochemistry, policy, broadband) who identified the reshoring opportunity through personal military-reserve experience rather than industry tenure. That outsider's-eye framing helped raise capital quickly, but the distributed-factory execution — hiring machinists, managing franchise quality, and scaling across five countries — is a fundamentally different skill set than the founder's prior ventures. Diligence should weight operating and manufacturing leadership hires heavily.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Accounts/programs | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Small-to-mid aerospace/defense component orders | 3,000 | $250,000 | $0.75bn | HCP assumption |
| Large defense primes and energy operators | 500 | $2.0m | $1.00bn | HCP assumption |
| Strategic national-security/government programs | 60 | $10.0m | $0.60bn | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | 3,560 |  | **$2.35bn** | Annual reshored precision-component revenue pool |
| HCP penetration |  |  | **7.5% of TAM revenue** | Roughly 135 operating factories by 2032 |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price after a very fast up-round:** the seed-to-Series-A price jump means a small check clears only a thin base MOIC and a clear downside loss. Invest only if a lower effective entry (secondary, later round at a flat or down valuation) becomes available.
- **Franchise-quality control:** distributed, partly franchised factories are inherently harder to keep consistent than a single company-operated site. Require site-level quality and delivery data across both models before committing.
- **Defense-industrial-base friction:** aerospace and defense supply-chain qualification is slow and relationship-driven; a software-first outsider may face longer sales and qualification cycles than the 25-factories-by-end-of-2026 plan implies.
- **Execution pace risk:** opening factories across five countries in under two years is aggressive; delays would directly compress the revenue build this model depends on.

## 89. Isometric

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Price-sensitive
**Links:** [Company](https://isometric.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://isometric.com/writing-articles/isometric-raises-40m-to-bring-agentic-certification-to-the-industrial-economy) | [TechFundingNews coverage](https://techfundingnews.com/isometric-40m-series-a-industrial-certification-ai/) | [Seed coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2023/07/17/isometric-taps-25m-to-build-a-registry-and-science-platform-focused-on-carbon-removal/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Eamon Jubbawy | Founder and CEO | Previously co-founded Onfido, a digital-identity verification company that verified over a billion identities before a $650m acquisition by Entrust — direct, relevant experience building a trust/verification infrastructure business to scale and exit. |
| Jennifer Wilcox | Chief Scientist (not a founder) | Former Principal Deputy Assistant Secretary at the U.S. Department of Energy; published foundational work on carbon dioxide removal. Listed as key leadership, not as a co-founder, on the company's own team page. |
| Stacy Kauk | Chief Science Officer (not a founder) | Former Head of Sustainability at Shopify and a founding member of Frontier (the carbon-removal offtake coalition); listed as key leadership, not as a co-founder. |

### Product description

Isometric operates Certify, an AI-agent-driven certification platform, alongside a public carbon-removal registry that gives buyers and suppliers access to project data, protocols, and issued carbon-removal certificates. Certify deploys AI agents to ingest and cross-check the data underlying a certification claim — sensor readings, satellite imagery, supply-chain records, and laboratory results — flagging inconsistencies and escalating cases that require expert human judgment. The company states this can compress certification timelines from roughly 12 months to hours. Isometric started with carbon-removal certification (biochar, enhanced weathering, direct air capture, reforestation, ocean alkalinity enhancement) and, with its June 2026 Series A, is expanding into broader industrial certification: embodied emissions in low-carbon steel and cement, superpollutant reductions, renewable energy certificates, and low-carbon shipping and aviation fuels. Disclosed customers/counterparties include Microsoft, Boeing, JPMorgan Chase, and Anglo American, with more than 16 million tonnes of carbon removal contracted across more than 200 projects.

### Thesis: why invest

Isometric raised a $40m Series A in June 2026, led by AVP (AXA Venture Partners) with global insurer AXA as anchor investor, and existing investors Lowercarbon Capital and Plural participating alongside personal investments from Kleiner Perkins chairman John Doerr and investor Walter Kortschak. This followed a $25m seed in July 2023 led by Lowercarbon Capital and Plural — total disclosed funding of $65m. The company's framing is compelling: the voluntary carbon market's credibility problems have stemmed partly from a "referees paid by the players" conflict of interest, where project developers historically paid for their own verification. Isometric flips that model so buyers fund certification, and backs it with AI-accelerated, evidence-linked verification rather than slow manual audits.

Jubbawy's Onfido track record (built and sold an identity-verification infrastructure company for $650m) is a direct, relevant precedent for building trust infrastructure that can scale to a large, diversified certification market. The disclosed customer list (Microsoft, Boeing, JPMorgan Chase, Anglo American) suggests real enterprise credibility beyond the carbon-removal niche the company started in.

**What must be true:** Certify's AI-driven verification must remain scientifically rigorous enough to satisfy skeptical corporate buyers and regulators as it expands beyond carbon removal into broader industrial certification; the buyer-pays model must not recreate its own conflict-of-interest concerns; and Isometric must win share from entrenched incumbents (Verra, Gold Standard) and well-funded specialist competitors (Puro.earth, BeZero Carbon, Sylvera) across multiple certification categories simultaneously.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed ARR (currently undisclosed), expansion of contracted volume beyond 16 million tonnes and beyond carbon removal into at least one additional industrial-certification category at meaningful scale, and a published, independently reviewed comparison of Certify's accuracy/consistency against traditional manual verification.

### Founder bet

The bet is on a repeat, high-credibility founder (Onfido's $650m exit) applying a proven verification-infrastructure playbook to a new, larger, and messier market. The team is unusually strong for this stage, with a Chief Scientist (ex-DOE) and Chief Science Officer (ex-Shopify, Frontier founding member) providing genuine scientific credibility alongside Jubbawy's commercial and infrastructure-building track record. The risk for HCP is not the team or the business — it is the price.

|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Isometric** | Buyer-funded certification/registry fees; carbon-removal and industrial buyers/suppliers | X AI-agent evidence verification, X public registry, X protocol development across CDR pathways | Cloud platform (Certify plus registry) | Buyer-funded model avoiding supplier-paid conflict of interest, plus AI-accelerated verification speed | Undisclosed | $40m Series A; $65m total; valuation undisclosed; AVP/AXA, Lowercarbon Capital, Plural, John Doerr, Walter Kortschak |
| Verra | Legacy carbon-credit registry/standard; project developers and buyers | X broad registry and methodology library; Partial modern AI-driven verification speed vs. Isometric | Registry/standard-setting body | Largest incumbent registry by historical volume and market recognition | Fee-based | Nonprofit/incumbent; capital structure not comparable |
| Gold Standard | Legacy carbon-credit registry/standard; project developers and buyers | X broad registry and methodology library; Partial modern AI-driven verification speed vs. Isometric | Registry/standard-setting body | Long-standing credibility, particularly for co-benefit-focused projects | Fee-based | Nonprofit/incumbent; capital structure not comparable |
| Puro.earth | CDR-focused registry; carbon-removal buyers and suppliers | X CDR-specific registry and methodologies; Partial buyer-funded model vs. Isometric | Registry platform | Early mover in engineered-CDR-specific registry standards | Fee-based | Private (Nasdaq-affiliated); capital data undisclosed here |

|---|---:|---|
