### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price is the binding constraint:** at an HCP-assumed $300m post-money, a $2.0m check buys too little ownership for a $1.0-2.5m check to clear a venture return bar even in Isometric's own strong base case. This is a "great company, wrong-sized check at this price" situation, not a business-quality problem. Pursue only via a smaller allocation, a secondary at a discount, or a structure (e.g., a SAFE with a valuation cap) that does not require competing for primary Series A allocation at the full disclosed round size.
- **Downside includes real capital loss:** at 60% of base revenue and one turn off the multiple, HCP's downside case falls below 1.0x MOIC. Confirm actual post-money valuation before committing any capital, since the entire return case is more sensitive to entry price than to operating performance.
- **Incumbent and specialist competition:** Verra and Gold Standard have decades of market recognition despite credibility criticism, while Puro.earth, BeZero Carbon, and Sylvera all compete for parts of the same buyer/verification relationship. Isometric must win share from all of them simultaneously across an expanding set of certification categories.
- **Expansion-execution risk:** moving from a carbon-removal-specific registry into broad industrial certification (steel, cement, aviation fuel) is a significant scope expansion announced concurrently with this round. Require evidence of traction in at least one non-carbon-removal category before assuming the larger TAM materializes.

## 90. Lindy

**Stage:** Series A (stale — see caveat)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://www.lindy.ai/) | [Funding dossier (third-party)](https://www.clay.com/dossier/lindy-funding) | [Founder interview and revenue detail](https://saasclub.io/podcast/lindy-flo-crivello-450/)

**Roster-swap note:** Lindy replaces Class Companion (classcompanion.com), which was acquired by Panorama Education on April 23, 2025 and is no longer an independent, fundable company. Lindy is the first-listed alternate for this batch.

**Stage caveat:** public sources materially disagree on Lindy's funding history and current stage. Third-party trackers describe a "$50m Series A" led by Battery Ventures (2023), while a funding dossier breaks the same aggregate $49.9m into a $3.9m seed, an $11m Series A, and a $35m tranche it separately labels a Series B, also led by Battery Ventures. A separate founder interview states that "most" of the company's total $52m came through predecessor company TeamFlow (which Flo Crivello pivoted away from in early 2023, cutting the team from roughly 50 to a third of that size) rather than through fresh capital raised specifically for Lindy. HCP could not resolve this discrepancy from public sources and treats Lindy's true current stage, cash position, and valuation as unconfirmed. No financing has been publicly reported since 2023.

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Flo Crivello | Founder and CEO | Founded TeamFlow, then pivoted the company to Lindy in early 2023 after a customer's offhand question ("can AI update Salesforce automatically?") led him to generalize the idea into a no-code AI agent platform; confirmed via multiple podcast interviews (SaaS Club, Chroma) and Notable Capital's interview series. |

### Product description

Lindy is a no-code platform for building and managing AI agents that automate business workflows — inbox management, meeting scheduling, calendar management, CRM updates, and ad hoc tasks across connected apps — without requiring engineering resources. It serves SMBs and startups (reportedly mostly five-to-100-person tech companies) across use cases spanning sales, marketing, operations, support, and recruiting. The company's own site claims more than 400,000 professionals use the product, with tiered pricing from $49.99 to $199.99 per month plus custom enterprise pricing. Product-market fit reportedly inflected sharply after a version 2.0 relaunch in May 2024, following a period the founder described as "pushing a boulder uphill."

### Thesis: why invest

The founder-interview evidence (SaaS Club podcast) describes "high seven figures" of revenue, a lean 35-person team plus contractors, and a capital-efficient operating posture — the company reportedly retained capital rather than spending aggressively after the TeamFlow pivot, cutting two-thirds of the original team to preserve runway while searching for product-market fit. A single March 2023 demo video reportedly generated 70,000 waitlist signups, and the company's homepage claims 400,000-plus professional users as of a May 2026 verification date cited in aggregator research. If accurate, this describes a capital-efficient, fast-growing company that has not needed to raise fresh institutional capital since 2023 — which is either a strong signal of default-alive economics or a sign that the company has been unable to raise on attractive terms. Public sources do not resolve which.

The category thesis (no-code AI agents for SMB workflow automation) is directly analogous to Mem0's memory-layer thesis in the reference file, but at the application layer rather than the infrastructure layer, and is correspondingly more exposed to competition from well-capitalized incumbents (Zapier, Microsoft Copilot Studio) extending into the same no-code agent-builder space.

**What must be true:** the reported "high seven figures" revenue must be confirmed and shown to be growing, not merely disclosed once in an interview; Lindy must clarify why it has not raised fresh capital since 2023 despite apparent growth; and the product must differentiate durably from Zapier's and Microsoft's own agent-builder pushes into the same SMB automation market.

**Next-round milestones:** a confirmed, disclosed financing event that resolves current valuation and cap-table ambiguity; $15m ARR; and a clear answer, obtained directly from the company, on why no institutional round has closed publicly in three years.

### Founder bet

Crivello's willingness to cut two-thirds of his own team and pivot an entire company rather than keep pushing a underperforming product is a real signal of founder discipline, and the subsequent inflection (as described in his own account) is consistent with genuine product-market fit rather than manufactured hype. However, the almost complete absence of independently verifiable, recent financial disclosure is a serious diligence gap that HCP cannot resolve from public sources alone.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Unresolved capitalization and valuation:** this is the single largest information gap in the batch. HCP's $220m post-money assumption is a wide-range guess, not a grounded estimate, and the base MOIC is highly sensitive to it. Do not proceed without a direct company conversation and a real cap table.
- **Stale financing signal:** three years without a confirmed institutional round is unusual for a company claiming strong growth. It may reflect capital efficiency or an inability to raise on attractive terms; these have opposite implications for underwriting.
- **Crowded category:** Zapier, Microsoft, and open-source alternatives (n8n) are all extending into no-code AI agent building, directly targeting Lindy's SMB customer base.
- **Why invest anyway:** the founder's demonstrated willingness to make a hard pivot and cut costs, combined with a credible "high seven figures" revenue claim and 400,000-plus claimed users, describes a real business. The recommendation is Watch, not Pass, because the underlying signal is genuinely interesting — but HCP should not commit capital until the financing and cap-table ambiguity is resolved directly with the company.

## 91. Basis

**Stage:** Series B (verified; roster hint said Series A, and the roster URL hint usebasis.co is incorrect — it resolves to an unrelated banking-data API company). Basis priced a $3.6m seed, a $34m Series A in December 2024, and a $100m Series B at a disclosed $1.15bn post-money on February 24, 2026. HCP keeps Basis in scope per the batch's Series-B exception, but recommends against pursuing at this price.
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://www.getbasis.ai/) | [Series B financing](https://siliconangle.com/2026/02/24/ai-accounting-startup-basis-secures-100m-1-15b-valuation-firms-adopt-agent-based-workflows/) | [Series A coverage](https://www.citybiz.co/article/640958/basis-raises-34m-to-advance-ai-agents-for-accounting/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Matt Harpe | Co-founder and CEO | SiliconANGLE's Series B coverage identifies Harpe as co-founder and CEO, with a prior background at Boston Consulting Group and SoftBank. |
| Zenna Tavares, Emily Mackevicius, Eli Bingham | Reported research co-founders | An industry newsletter (nextplayso.substack.com) identifies these three as Basis's founding research team — Tavares an innovation scholar at Columbia's Zuckerman Institute, Mackevicius a postdoctoral researcher in memory science, and Bingham a former Uber AI Labs scientist and Pyro probabilistic-programming co-creator. This is not confirmed on Basis's own site in materials reviewed; confirm current roles and equity in diligence. |

### Product description

Basis builds autonomous AI agents that perform accounting work end-to-end — tax preparation, audit testing, reconciliation, and document review — for professional accounting firms and in-house accounting departments. The company positions the product as "unified accounting intelligence" rather than a simple chatbot: agents operate independently for extended periods on defined workflows and hand off to human accountants at critical decision points, adapting to firm-specific engagement contexts over time. As of the Series B, Basis reported that approximately 30% of the Top 25 U.S. accounting firms use its agents across client accounting services, tax, and audit practices, with named customers including Boulay PLLP, Clark Nuber PS, MarksNelson LLC, Pinion LLC, and UHY LLC.

### Thesis: why invest

Basis has raised aggressively and successfully: a $3.6m seed, a $34m Series A in December 2024 led by Khosla Ventures (with NFDG, and individual investors including OpenAI board members Larry Summers and Adam D'Angelo, and Google's Jeff Dean), and a $100m Series B on February 24, 2026 at a disclosed $1.15bn post-money, led by Accel and Google Ventures with Lloyd Blankfein, Khosla Ventures, NFDG, Better Tomorrow Ventures, Box Group, and Avid Ventures participating — alongside notable individual backers including Replit's Amjad Masad and Hugging Face's Clem Delangue. Roughly 30% of the Top 25 U.S. accounting firms using the product is a genuinely strong enterprise-adoption signal for a company at this stage, in a labor-constrained professional-services market.

The business is real and the operating momentum is credible. The problem for a $1.0m-$2.5m check is entirely about price: at a $1.15bn post-money, HCP's return model — even using a premium exit multiple relative to accounting-software peers — produces a base-case MOIC near 1.0x. This is a business to track for a later round or a structured/secondary entry, not a fit for a small primary check today.

**What must be true (for HCP's price concern to be wrong):** Basis would need to sustain hyper-growth well beyond what accounting-software public comps historically command, capture a dominant share of Top 400 U.S. firms, and expand into adjacent professional-services verticals (legal, financial advisory) fast enough to justify a multiple materially above the peer set HCP used.

**Next-round milestones (for re-underwriting at a future price):** 50%+ of Top 25 firms live, expansion into Top 400 firms at meaningful scale, disclosed ARR, and evidence gross margin holds above 70% as agent usage scales across firms with heterogeneous engagement types.

### Founder bet

Matt Harpe's BCG/SoftBank background brings commercial and scaling experience; the reported research co-founders (Tavares, Mackevicius, Bingham) bring genuine machine-learning research depth (Uber AI Labs, Pyro, computational neuroscience) that is credible technical grounding for a company claiming "unified accounting intelligence" rather than templated automation. The investor roster — sitting OpenAI board members, Google's chief scientist, and a former Goldman Sachs CEO all writing personal checks — is an unusually strong insider-conviction signal, even though it does not change HCP's price-driven conclusion for a small check today.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Large / regional CPA firms (>$10m revenue) | 2,000 | $150,000 | $300m | HCP assumption: enterprise-wide agent deployment across audit, tax, CAS |
| Mid-size CPA firms ($1m-$10m revenue) | 8,000 | $40,000 | $320m | HCP assumption |
| Small firms and sole practitioners (<$1m revenue) | 35,000 | $10,000 | $350m | HCP assumption; lighter self-serve SKU |
| **TAM** | 45,000 | | **$970m** | Annual U.S. accounting-firm software pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **41.2% of TAM revenue** | Reflects the disclosed ~30%-of-Top-25 adoption already achieved, extended to broader firm tiers |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Price:** at a $1.15bn post-money, even a strong operating outcome (upside case: 150% of base revenue, one turn higher multiple) produces roughly 2.2x — well short of a venture return for a $1.0m-$2.5m check. This is the primary reason for the Pass; it is not a judgment on the underlying business.
- **Concentration in Top 25 firms:** the headline 30% adoption figure is among the 25 largest U.S. accounting firms; expansion into the much larger Top 400 and mid-size firm population (where most of HCP's TAM sits) is unproven at scale.
- **Founder-team confirmation:** the research-team founder claims (Tavares, Mackevicius, Bingham) come from a secondary source, not Basis's own materials. Confirm current roles and cap-table participation directly.
- **Why track anyway:** if HCP can access a later, larger fund vehicle, a structured secondary at a discount to $1.15bn, or a smaller strategic check tied to a specific partnership, Basis's underlying adoption metrics (30% of Top 25 firms, tier-one insider investor roster) are strong enough to merit continued monitoring for a different entry structure.

## 92. Ello

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://www.ello.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.globenewswire.com/news-release/2023/09/07/2739711/0/en/Ello-World-s-Most-Advanced-AI-Reading-Coach-Raises-15M-Series-A.html) | [TechCrunch coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2023/09/07/ai-reading-coach-startup-ello-raises-15-million-to-bolster-child-literacy/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Tom Sayer | Co-founder and CEO | Previously led impact and adoption programs at Google for Education, ensuring effective classroom tool usage globally, per company and podcast profiles. |
| Dr. Elizabeth Adams | Co-founder and Chief Experience Officer | Clinical psychologist specializing in child development and behavior; multiple interviews (Pulse2, Jack Hammer) profile her role shaping Ello's pedagogy. |
| Catalin Voss | Co-founder and CTO | AI researcher, PhD candidate in AI at Stanford working on social-good applications and digital therapies for developmental conditions; co-founded and sold two prior ML startups (DukaConnect, Sension). |

### Product description

Ello is an AI reading coach for children roughly ages 4-9 that listens to a child read aloud from real physical books, using child-specific speech recognition to catch and gently correct errors in real time, similar to how a parent or tutor would sit beside a child during reading practice. The company has claimed its speech-recognition model outperforms OpenAI's Whisper and Google Cloud's speech API on children's speech specifically — a claim HCP has not independently verified. The subscription product ships a set of physical books to families each month (reported at five books for $24.99/month in third-party pricing summaries) alongside the app-based reading-coach experience.

### Thesis: why invest

Ello raised a $15m Series A in September 2023 led by Goodwater Capital, with Homebrew (returning), Reed Hastings, Common Sense Growth, and Ravensburger as major participants, and Project A, Y Combinator, WndrCo, Reach Capital, Visible Ventures, and Khosla Ventures also involved — a genuinely strong, literacy- and education-focused investor syndicate. At the time, third-party coverage cited roughly 10,000 families using the product and more than 300,000 books read on the app. No financing has been publicly confirmed since that September 2023 round, nearly three years before this memo.

The founding team's combination — an ex-Google-for-Education operator, a clinical child-development psychologist, and an AI researcher with two prior ML exits — is genuinely strong and well-matched to the specific problem of child literacy. That team quality is the best argument for the business. But the public record HCP can access shows no evidence of growth, revenue, or user-base updates since the Series A round closed, and the specific, narrow claim (child speech recognition beating Whisper and Google Cloud) is exactly the kind of capability increasingly commoditized by general-purpose model improvements from the same providers Ello claims to beat.

**What must be true:** the company must have continued growing materially since 2023 (unconfirmed publicly); its speech-recognition advantage must remain durable as OpenAI's and Google's own models improve at children's-speech transcription specifically; and the physical-book subscription logistics must scale profitably rather than acting as a permanent drag on gross margin.

**Next-round milestones:** a confirmed, disclosed financing event; 100,000 paying families; $20m ARR; and independent, third-party validation of the speech-recognition accuracy claim against current-generation general models.

### Founder bet

This is the strongest founding team on a pure-credentials basis in the batch — a rare match of pedagogical, clinical, and technical expertise to a well-defined problem. The recommendation below is not a comment on the team; it reflects that HCP cannot verify continued momentum, and the modeled return at any defensible entry price is weak given the comp set and the real risk that a narrow, provider-beatable AI capability erodes over a seven-year hold.

### Competitive landscape

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Stale financing and unknown momentum:** nearly three years without a confirmed round, with no public revenue, user, or growth updates since the Series A, is a serious gap. HCP cannot distinguish "quietly growing and capital-efficient" from "struggled to raise a follow-on" from public sources.
- **Erodible technical moat:** the specific claimed advantage (beating Whisper and Google's own speech APIs on children's speech) is precisely the kind of narrow capability general-purpose model providers are most likely to close over a multi-year hold.
- **Weak comp-set economics:** consumer edtech subscription businesses, illustrated starkly by Chegg's 0.24x multiple, face real structural skepticism from public markets about AI-driven disruption of their own category.
- **Downside case falls below 1.0x:** the modeled downside MOIC (0.57x) means a plausible, not merely a tail-risk, scenario loses HCP money outright. Given the financing staleness and erosion risk above, HCP recommends passing at this stage rather than paying to find out; revisit only if the company can show confirmed, recent growth and a defensible speech-recognition moat.

## 93. Orbital Materials

**Stage:** Series B (screened at Series A per roster)
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company (now Orbital Industries)](https://www.orbitalindustries.com/) | [Series A report](https://techcrunch.com/2024/02/21/this-startup-is-using-ai-to-discover-new-materials/) | [Series B report](https://fortune.com/2026/05/28/exclusive-orbital-industries-raises-50-million-series-b-funding-round-ai-to-discover-exotic-new-materials/)

### Stage-progression and rebrand note

Orbital Materials was assigned to this batch as a Series A company. Since its $16m Series A closed in February 2024, the company has rebranded to **Orbital Industries** and raised a $50m Series B (reported by Fortune, May 2026) led by Plural. This memo underwrites the company under its current name and stage, consistent with the instruction that a Series B company may be retained with an explained exception; the current website (orbitalindustries.com) does not itself narrate the rebrand, so the name change is sourced to third-party press coverage rather than a company statement.

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Jonathan Godwin | Co-founder and CEO | Previously a senior materials-science researcher at DeepMind; holds an MSc in Machine Learning from UCL and a BA in Mathematics and Philosophy from the University of Bristol. |
| James Gin-Pollock | Co-founder | Named as a co-founder in company-founding coverage; individual background not independently detailed in sources reviewed here. |
| Daniel Miodovnik | Co-founder | Named as a co-founder in company-founding coverage; individual background not independently detailed in sources reviewed here. |

### Product description

Orbital (Materials/Industries) builds LINUS, an AI foundation model for materials science trained on public materials data, computer simulations, and the company's own wet-lab experiments. Users can prompt the model in natural language — for example, requesting "a material that has good absorption for carbon dioxide" — and LINUS generates candidate 3D molecular structures. The company then develops promising candidates through to proof-of-concept or pilot stage in its own labs (London and a newer New Jersey wet lab) and partners with external manufacturers to scale production rather than manufacturing at scale itself, which is a materially less capital-intensive model than Daedalus's or Isembard's owned-factory approaches. Its first disclosed product application is a lower-cost, more reliable sorbent/filter for capturing carbon dioxide from the air; the current site also references work in data-center cooling materials.

### Thesis: why invest

Orbital's core wager — that a frontier-AI-trained materials-discovery model can compress years of trial-and-error chemistry into a software-driven design loop — is directionally similar to how AlphaFold-style models changed structural biology, and Jonathan Godwin's direct DeepMind materials-science research background is a credible, verifiable qualification for that specific bet. The company has attracted a strong and unusual investor set across rounds, including Radical Ventures and Toyota Ventures at Series A and, per company materials, NVIDIA's NVentures; the Series B was led by Plural.

The commercial case is, however, thinner than the technical story. Public sources reviewed here do not disclose named paying customers, revenue, or the commercial terms of the carbon-capture sorbent partnership; the company's own materials describe a pipeline of candidate materials rather than confirmed commercial deployments. Combined with a Series B entry price, this makes Orbital a name to track closely rather than commit meaningful capital to today.

**What must be true:** at least one AI-discovered material must reach commercial-scale production and generate disclosed licensing or product revenue; the discovery-to-commercialization cycle time must compress materially versus traditional materials R&D, not just at the discovery stage; and manufacturing partners must be willing to scale unproven materials from a young company.

**Next-round milestones:** at least one named, revenue-generating commercial partnership (ideally the carbon-capture product), disclosed revenue or licensing-fee figures, a second validated material class beyond carbon capture, and clarity on the rebrand's implications for company strategy and the data-center-cooling product line now visible on the company's site.

### Founder bet

The bet is on a technically elite, DeepMind-trained founder applying a genuinely novel AI-for-science approach to an industry (specialty materials) that has historically been slow to adopt software-native methods. The risk is the classic hard-tech translation gap: strong research credentials and investor enthusiasm do not guarantee that AI-discovered materials clear the cost, regulatory, and manufacturing-partner hurdles required to become real product revenue. Diligence should ask directly for the commercial status of the carbon-capture product and any other named pipeline material.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Partnerships/accounts | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Mid-market specialty-chemical/materials licensing partners | 250 | $2.0m | $500m | HCP assumption |
| Large industrial partners (batteries, semiconductors, decarbonization) | 80 | $10.0m | $800m | HCP assumption |
| Strategic global/national materials programs | 20 | $30.0m | $600m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | 350 |  | **$1.90bn** | Annual AI-discovered-materials licensing/royalty pool |
| HCP penetration |  |  | **7.9% of TAM revenue** | Roughly 34 commercialized material partnerships by 2032 |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** |  |  | **$150m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Commercialized material partnerships | 4 | 8 | 13 | 19 | 25 | 30 | 34 |
| Avg. annual revenue/partnership | $1.4m | $2.0m | $2.5m | $3.0m | $3.4m | $3.7m | $4.4m |
| **Revenue** | **6** | **16** | **33** | **57** | **85** | **111** | **150** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / use | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Orbital (Materials/Industries)** | AI foundation model for materials discovery | X candidate generation; Partial commercial scale-up (manufacturing via partners) | Software model + own wet lab + manufacturing partnerships | DeepMind-caliber research talent; experimentally validated model outputs | Undisclosed | $50m Series B (May 2026), ~$70m+ total; Plural, Radical Ventures, Toyota Ventures, NVentures |
| Citrine Informatics | AI-driven materials-informatics platform | X candidate screening; Partial own-lab validation | Software platform sold to materials companies | Long operating history and enterprise customer base | Enterprise licensing | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Lila Sciences (formerly Genesis Mission-adjacent AI-science labs) | AI-driven scientific discovery across domains | Partial materials-specific depth; X broad AI-science platform | Software + lab | Broad AI-for-science platform and capital | Undisclosed | Private; large late-stage rounds; valuation not used here |
| Recursion Pharmaceuticals (biology, not materials) | AI-native drug discovery platform | No evidence materials-specific; X AI discovery workflow for biology | Software + own wet lab | Public-market scale and large discovery dataset | N/A (biotech pipeline) | Public; included as an AI-native-discovery business-model analogue, not a direct materials comp |
| Traditional specialty-chemical R&D (BASF, Dow internal labs) | In-house materials R&D | X production and scale; No evidence AI-native discovery speed | Internal R&D + manufacturing | Decades of manufacturing scale and customer relationships | Not applicable | Public; not directly comparable at deal stage |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Recursion Pharmaceuticals](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/rxrx/statistics/) | 14.77x | AI-native scientific-discovery business model, different end market (biology); included for directional context, not the median |
| [Ecovyst](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/ecvt/statistics/) | 2.12x | Specialty catalysts and materials |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **No disclosed commercial revenue:** every revenue figure in this memo is an HCP assumption; the company has not disclosed a paying customer or licensing deal in the sources reviewed. Treat this as a name to revisit once real commercial data exists, not a current-quarter commitment.
- **Entry price:** at an assumed $240m post-Series-B post-money, a $2.0m check produces an approximately break-even base case and a clear downside loss. This is the central reason for the Watch rating rather than Diligence or Pursue.
- **Hard-tech translation risk:** AI-discovered materials must still clear real-world manufacturing, cost, and regulatory hurdles that no amount of model quality alone resolves. Require evidence of at least one material in actual production, not just lab validation.
- **Strategy ambiguity post-rebrand:** the shift from "Orbital Materials" to "Orbital Industries" and the appearance of a data-center-cooling product line suggest a broader, possibly less focused strategy than the original cleantech-materials thesis. Clarify the company's current product priorities before diligence proceeds further.

## 94. 222

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $2.0m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://222.place/) | [Series A report](https://www.fastcompany.com/91356813/222-aims-to-end-loneliness-by-engineering-chance) | [Company profile](https://www.ycombinator.com/companies/222)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Danial Hashemi | Co-founder | Fast Company and Y Combinator identify Hashemi as one of three co-founders; company founded in 2023. |
| Keyan Kazemian | Co-founder | Named alongside Hashemi and Roshannai as a founder in Fast Company's reporting. |
| Arman Roshannai | Co-founder | Named alongside Hashemi and Kazemian as a founder in Fast Company's reporting. |

### Product description

222 is an AI-driven platform that arranges in-person social experiences — dinners, comedy shows, and similar small-group activities — for strangers matched by a personality assessment rather than profile browsing. The product deliberately excludes the swiping, DM, and public-profile mechanics common to dating and networking apps; instead, users complete an assessment and are algorithmically placed into curated groups (the company references "5 close matches") for booked, real-world experiences at local venues. Founded in 2023 by Hashemi, Kazemian, and Roshannai, the 16-person, New York City-based company has expanded from an initial Los Angeles launch into New York.

### Thesis: why invest

222 raised a $10.1m Series A led by Upfront Ventures (partner Mark Suster), with Pioneer Fund, Y Combinator, General Catalyst, Offline Ventures, Greg Isenberg, and Dropbox co-founder Arash Ferdowsi participating, per Fast Company's reporting — a strong, credible investor syndicate for a company at this stage. The round followed an earlier $2.5m seed reported by Dealroom. 222 sits squarely in the same "AI-matched IRL connection" category as Pie and Timeleft elsewhere in this batch, competing on a similar loneliness/social-isolation thesis with an emphasis on algorithmic matching quality over browsing UX.

The investor quality (Upfront, General Catalyst, YC, and a well-known angel roster) is a genuine positive signal, but HCP found no disclosed pricing, revenue, or user-scale metrics on the company's own site or in press coverage — this is an earlier-stage, thinner-evidence file than Timeleft (which has real disclosed ARR) or even Pie (which has disclosed MAU figures). 222's public footprint is currently the smallest of the three IRL-matching companies in this batch.

**What must be true:** the AI matching engine must produce measurably better group compatibility than simpler heuristics (shared interests, availability, location) that competitors could replicate cheaply; the New York expansion must show it can replicate LA-market traction; and a monetization model must emerge and be disclosed.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed monthly participant volume and pricing, expansion beyond LA and NY, evidence of repeat participation, and a clear revenue model with early unit economics.

### Founder bet

Three co-founders building a company through Y Combinator, with a credible institutional syndicate behind the Series A, is a reasonable starting signal, but HCP has less public information on the founders' prior backgrounds than for other companies in this batch. Diligence should establish founder track records directly.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| US urban singles/professionals seeking curated IRL matching | 18m | $50 | $900m | HCP assumption |
| Corporate/community event partnerships | — | — | $100m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$1.0bn** | Annual net-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **6.0% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$60m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **3** | **7** | **14** | **24** | **36** | **48** | **60** |

222 has disclosed no revenue or pricing publicly. This table is an HCP construction, not a company projection.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **222** | AI-matched curated IRL experiences | X matching, event booking; No evidence monetization disclosed | Mobile app, 2-city footprint (LA, NYC) | AI personality-assessment matching engine | Undisclosed | $10.1m Series A; $2.5m seed prior; Upfront Ventures, Pioneer Fund, YC, General Catalyst, Offline Ventures |
| Timeleft | Scheduled stranger-dinner matching | X matching and weekly recurring events; 200+-city footprint | Mobile app | Disclosed real revenue and much larger city footprint | Per-event fee | $7m Series A (see this batch's Timeleft memo) |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | High-engagement consumer-discovery comp |
| [Bumble](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/bmbl/statistics/) | 0.85x | Social-matching consumer comp |
| [Eventbrite](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/eb/statistics/) | 0.77x | In-person-event infrastructure comp |
| **Median** | **0.85x** | HCP uses 1.0x, near median given the earliest-stage evidence in this batch's IRL-social sub-group |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $50m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 4.00% ($2.0m / $50m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 2.60% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $60m / 1.0x |
| Exit enterprise value | $60m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $1.56m / **0.78x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.468x / 2.34x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($36m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (already at the 1.0x floor, so unchanged) yields $36m EV, $0.936m proceeds, 0.468x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($90m) at 2.0x yields $180m EV, $4.68m proceeds, 2.34x MOIC.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Thinnest evidence base in the IRL-social sub-group:** no disclosed pricing, revenue, or scale metrics anywhere HCP could find. Require a data room with basic operating metrics before further diligence.
- **Category crowding:** Timeleft and Pie are both pursuing closely related theses with more disclosed traction. 222 must show clear differentiation beyond "also AI-matched."
- **Two-city concentration:** all known operations are LA and NYC. Confirm expansion plans and early performance data from any additional markets.
- **Why watch rather than pass:** the investor syndicate (Upfront, General Catalyst, YC, a credible angel roster) is a real quality signal that HCP would not want to dismiss without first requesting basic operating data — the company may simply be earlier and quieter publicly than its peers, not weaker.

---

## 95. Eve

**Stage:** Series B (verified; roster hint said Series A). Eve priced a $47m Series A in January 2025 and a $103m Series B at a disclosed "$1 billion" post-money valuation on September 30, 2025; HCP keeps Eve in scope per the batch's Series-B exception, but recommends against pursuing at this price.
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://www.eve.legal/) | [Series A financing](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/eve-secures-47-million-to-fuel-era-of-ai-native-law-firms-302353165.html) | [Series B financing](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/eve-raises-103-million-at-1-billion-valuation-to-help-plaintiff-firms-deliver-justice-through-ai-transformation-302570807.html)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Jay (Jayanth) Madheswaran | Co-founder and CEO | 15+ years in AI/ML at Facebook and Rubrik (first engineer and head of product engineering); previously at Lightspeed Venture Partners, which later co-led Eve's Series A. |
| Matt Noe | Co-founder and Chief Product Officer | Founding engineer at Rubrik with roughly a decade of AI product-development experience alongside Madheswaran. |
| David Zeng | Co-founder and Chief Architect / Head of Engineering | 10+ years of AI and machine-learning experience, per Eve's company page. |

### Product description

Eve is an AI platform purpose-built for plaintiff law firms (personal injury and labor/employment practices), covering case intake and evaluation, medical chronologies and case overviews, legal document and demand-letter drafting, and discovery management (both propounding and responding), delivered through what the company calls the "EveOS" platform along with an AI auditor and communications agent. The pitch is that AI-native plaintiff firms can represent more clients with the same headcount by automating the document- and data-heavy parts of case preparation, letting attorneys focus on strategy and advocacy.

### Thesis: why invest

Eve raised a $47m Series A on January 16, 2025, led by Andreessen Horowitz with Lightspeed and Menlo Ventures participating; the announcement reported more than 100 firms using the platform and 500% year-over-year revenue growth, with named customers including Mike Morse Law Firm, Atlanta Personal Injury Law Group, Barrett & Farahany, and Frontier Law Center. Just eight and a half months later, on September 30, 2025, Eve raised a $103m Series B at a disclosed "$1 billion" post-money valuation, led by Spark Capital with a16z, Lightspeed, and Menlo returning — an exceptionally fast unicorn transition that reflects genuine investor conviction in the plaintiff-law vertical.

The moat, if durable, is case-outcome and workflow data specific to plaintiff practice — medical chronology patterns, demand-letter structures, and discovery workflows that compound as more firms route more cases through the platform. The problem, as with Basis in this batch, is entirely about price for a small check: at a $1bn+ entry, HCP's return model produces a sub-1.0x base-case MOIC even with a reasonably optimistic revenue and multiple assumption.

**What must be true (for HCP's price concern to be wrong):** Eve would need to become the dominant AI platform across a large majority of the plaintiff-firm market, sustain the 500%+ growth rate (or a high multiple of it) for several more years, and command an exit multiple well above the legal-tech public-comp set HCP used, none of which is established by public evidence today.

**Next-round milestones (for re-underwriting at a future price):** disclosed ARR, 500+ firms live, expansion beyond personal injury/labor into additional plaintiff-side practice areas, and evidence that case-outcome data creates measurable, defensible product advantages over newer entrants.

### Founder bet

Madheswaran, Noe, and Zeng share a Rubrik/Facebook AI-engineering pedigree, and Madheswaran's prior seat at Lightspeed (which co-led the Series A) suggests strong pre-existing investor relationships. This is a credible, technically deep founding team building into a real, underserved vertical (plaintiff law firms are notoriously under-resourced relative to case volume). The team quality is not in question; the entry price for a small check is.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Large national plaintiff / mass-tort firms | 500 | $300,000 | $150m | HCP assumption |
| Mid-size regional plaintiff firms | 5,000 | $50,000 | $250m | HCP assumption |

|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Eve** | AI platform for plaintiff law firms | X case intake, medical chronologies, drafting, discovery | Cloud (EveOS platform) | Case-outcome and workflow data specific to plaintiff practice | Undisclosed | $103m Series B at "$1 billion" valuation; $150m total; Spark, a16z, Lightspeed, Menlo |

| Josef | No-code legal automation | Partial intake/workflow automation; No evidence of plaintiff-specific medical chronology tooling | Cloud | Law-firm-configurable automation builder | Custom | Private; capital data undisclosed here |
| Filevine | Legal case-management software | X case management; Partial AI-native drafting | Cloud | Broad plaintiff/PI firm installed base | Subscription | Private; valuation not used |
| Litify | Legal case-management platform (built on Salesforce) | X case management; Partial AI features | Cloud, Salesforce-native | Salesforce-platform distribution | Subscription | Private; capital data undisclosed here |

### Public comps and exit model

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Price:** at a $1bn+ post-money, base-case MOIC is below 1.0x, and even the upside case (150% of base revenue, one turn higher multiple) only reaches roughly 1.35x. This is a clear, price-driven Pass for a primary $1.0m-$2.5m check.
- **Aggressive TAM penetration assumption:** HCP's 44% base-case TAM penetration is high by this batch's standards and should be treated skeptically pending real competitive-response data from EvenUp, Alexi, and Thomson Reuters CoCounsel.
- **Vertical concentration:** revenue is concentrated in personal injury and labor/employment plaintiff practice; expansion into other plaintiff-side verticals (mass tort, product liability) is unproven publicly.
- **Why track anyway:** the founding team's technical pedigree (Facebook/Rubrik), the 500% disclosed YoY growth at Series A, and back-to-back top-tier lead investors (a16z then Spark) are all genuine positives. If HCP can access a later fund vehicle or a structured/secondary entry at a meaningful discount to $1bn, Eve merits continued monitoring.

## 96. Fay

**Stage:** Series B (exception — see roster notes above; roster hint listed Series A)
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://www.faynutrition.com/) | [Series A announcement](https://www.faynutrition.com/post/fay-emerges-with-25m-in-funding) | [Series B announcement](https://www.faynutrition.com/post/fay-series-b-announcement) | [Forerunner Ventures investment note](https://www.forerunnerventures.com/perspectives/how-fay-is-scaling-customized-nutrition-care-for-consumers-while-reshaping)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Sammy Faycurry | Co-founder and CEO | Built the platform initially for his mother and sister, both registered dietitians, per the company's own funding-announcement post. |
| Mark Stefanski | Co-founder and CTO | Co-built Fay's marketplace and insurance-billing technology alongside Faycurry. |

### Product description

Fay is a marketplace connecting patients with registered dietitian nutritionists (RDNs) for insurance-covered nutrition counseling, serving three sides of the market: patients (who pay $0 per session in-network with a covered plan), independent dietitians (who get a platform for practice-building, scheduling, and especially insurance billing — historically one of the biggest operational barriers to independent dietitian practice), and insurance partners. The company describes itself as a "digitally native franchise" model. As of its Series A announcement, Fay had more than 1,000 dietitians on the platform across 30+ specialties (eating disorders, diabetes, weight management, and others) and had signed partnerships with major insurers including UnitedHealthcare, Aetna CVS, Blue Cross, Anthem, Cigna, Optum, and Humana, giving it disclosed reach to more than 100 million Americans through those plans.

### Thesis: why invest

Fay's underlying business is genuinely strong: automating insurance billing for independent dietitians removes one of the largest real barriers to that profession's economic viability, and pairing that with a payer-covered, $0-copay consumer experience is a credible wedge into a large, underpenetrated category (nutrition counseling is broadly under-consumed relative to its evidence-based value for diabetes, obesity, and GI conditions). The company built this into a real, insurer-diversified network at reasonable capital efficiency through its Series A.

The problem for this specific memo is entirely price. Fay raised a $20m Series A (Forerunner Ventures, General Catalyst, 1984) in 2024, then closed a **$50m Series B led by Goldman Sachs at a disclosed $500m post-money valuation** in February 2025 — a fivefold valuation step-up in under a year, bringing total funding to $75m. At $500m post-money, even a strong, fully executed operating outcome for Fay does not clear a venture-acceptable return for a $1.0-2.5m check at this entry price, because the company's public comp set (marketplace and value-based-care peers) trades at EV/LTM revenue multiples far below what a $500m entry price implies is achievable. This is the clearest, most price-driven "Pass" case in the batch: the business may well be good, but the price is not investable at HCP's check size and return targets absent a materially different entry structure (a secondary at a real discount, a structured instrument, or participation at a much smaller allocation purely for portfolio/relationship reasons).

**What must be true:** Fay's actual current ARR would need to already be running at a premium multiple to its comp set to justify the $500m post-money (i.e., the market is pricing Fay more like a high-growth SaaS platform than a services marketplace) — this should be tested directly against disclosed or diligenced revenue figures, not assumed; and any future round would need to hold or grow the valuation for existing holders not to face dilution-adjusted value erosion.

**Next-round milestones (for monitoring only, not underwriting a Pass):** $100m+ ARR, expansion of the insurer network beyond the current seven-plus national payers, demonstrated dietitian-supply elasticity (network growing faster than churn), and a Series C or growth round that holds or exceeds the $500m valuation, which would be the clearest external validation that the price was justified.

### Founder bet

Sammy Faycurry's founding story — building the product for family members who are themselves dietitians — is a credible, close-to-the-problem origin, and the company's execution (1,000+ dietitians, seven-plus national payer partnerships, two funding rounds in quick succession from top-tier investors including Forerunner and Goldman Sachs) is genuinely strong by any objective standard. This memo's negative recommendation reflects price, not team or business quality — a distinction diligence notes should make explicit so the "Pass" is not misread as a judgment on the company itself.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Eligible adults | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Insured US adults with conditions warranting reimbursed nutrition counseling (diabetes, prediabetes, obesity, GI, eating disorders) | 40m | $100 | $4.00bn | HCP assumption: blended average of a small number of reimbursed visits per year at typical negotiated rates |
| **TAM** | 40m | | **$4.00bn** | Annual reimbursed nutrition-counseling revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **5.5% of TAM revenue** | Reflects continued national payer expansion and dietitian-network growth |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$220m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Paid dietitian network | 1,800 | 2,300 | 2,900 | 3,600 | 4,400 | 5,300 | 6,300 |
| Net platform revenue/dietitian | $31k | $30k | $32k | $33k | $34k | $35k | $35k |
| **Revenue** | **$56** | **$69** | **$93** | **$119** | **$150** | **$186** | **$221** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / use | Workflow coverage | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Fay** | Insurance-covered dietitian marketplace | X matching, scheduling, insurance billing | Web/app, national payer network | Insurance-billing automation for independent dietitians plus payer breadth | $0/session in-network | $50m Series B at $500m post-money valuation (disclosed); $75m total; Goldman Sachs, Forerunner, General Catalyst |
| Berry Street | Insurance-covered dietitian marketplace | X matching, scheduling, insurance billing | Web/app, national payer network | Direct competitor with a similar insurance-billing wedge; also disclosed a $50m raise around the same period per public reporting | $0/session in-network | Private; capital data undisclosed here beyond the disclosed $50m raise reported alongside Fay's |
| Nourish | Insurance-covered dietitian marketplace | X matching, scheduling, insurance billing | Web/app, national payer network | Rapidly scaled dietitian network per public reporting | $0/session in-network | Private; valuation undisclosed |
| Foodsmart | Employer/payer-sponsored nutrition and telehealth benefit | X nutrition counseling; Partial broader food-as-medicine services | Employer/payer-sponsored platform | Broader food-as-medicine positioning beyond 1:1 counseling | Employer/payer-paid | Private; valuation not used |
| Season Health | Food-as-medicine and nutrition benefits platform | Partial dietitian marketplace; X broader grocery/meal-delivery integration | Employer/payer-sponsored platform | Integrated food-delivery component | Employer/payer-paid | Private; valuation undisclosed |
| Traditional in-network RDN private practices | In-person/telehealth nutrition counseling | X counseling; X billing automation (typically manual/in-house) | In-person/telehealth, individual practices | Existing local patient relationships | Insurance-billed | Fragmented incumbent base; not independently comparable |

**Position:** Fay is a genuine category leader in insurance-covered dietitian marketplaces, competing most directly with Berry Street and Nourish in a space that has attracted real investor enthusiasm (Fierce Healthcare reported Fay and Berry Street each banking roughly $50m around the same period). The category risk for this memo is not competitive — it is that the entire category, including Fay specifically, may be priced for an outcome the underlying reimbursement economics cannot support at scale.

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Progyny](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pgny/statistics/) | 1.78x | Benefits marketplace connecting patients to specialized care, closest business-model analog |
| [Privia Health](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/prva/statistics/) | 1.33x | Physician-enablement network model; reused from HCP reference memo |
| [Accolade](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/accd/statistics/) | 1.32x | Care-navigation and benefits platform |
| [agilon health](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/agl/statistics/) | 0.34x | Value-based, network-dependent care model, depressed multiple |
| **Median** | **1.33x** | HCP uses 2.0x, above median to reflect Fay's stronger growth profile, but the disclosed $500m entry price is priced well above what even this premium multiple supports at realistic exit revenue |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $500m, disclosed (Goldman Sachs-led Series B, February 2025) |
| Initial ownership | 0.30% |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 0.20% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $220m / 2.0x |
| Exit enterprise value | $440m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $0.9m / **0.6x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.2x / 1.3x |

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price exceeds a supportable exit value at this memo's base case:** the modeled 2032 exit enterprise value ($440m) is below the current $500m post-money valuation. This is not a risk to mitigate through diligence; it is a structural reason to pass at the disclosed terms.
- **Even the upside case barely returns capital:** the modeled upside MOIC is approximately 1.3x. Any allocation to Fay should only be considered via a secondary at a meaningful discount to $500m, a structured instrument, or a much smaller check sized purely for strategic/relationship reasons, not as a standard $1.0-2.5m venture check.
- **Category crowding at the top:** Berry Street and Nourish are well-funded direct competitors in the same insurance-billing-automation wedge, per public reporting. Even if Fay wins the category, category economics (low per-visit reimbursement, thin marketplace take rates) may cap achievable multiples regardless of market-share outcome.
- **Why this memo still documents Fay in full:** the underlying business and team are genuinely strong, and terms can change — a future down round, secondary opportunity, or structured deal could make Fay investable again. This memo preserves the full underwriting so HCP can revisit quickly if pricing resets.

## 97. Yope

**Stage:** Seed *(swap-in for Flagship — see note at top of file)*
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Watch
**Links:** [Company](https://yope.app/) | [Seed report](https://techcrunch.com/2025/02/24/yope-is-sparking-genz-and-vc-interest-with-an-instagram-like-app-for-private-groups/) | [Independent profile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YOPE)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Bahram Ismailau | Co-founder and CEO | TechCrunch identifies Ismailau as CEO and co-founder; he and Rudkouski met studying together at Belarusian State University. |
| Paul Rudkouski | Co-founder | Named alongside Ismailau as co-founder; the pair worked together for years on prior products before Yope, per TechCrunch. |

### Product description

Yope is a private, feed-less photo-sharing app for small, trusted friend groups — deliberately positioned against public, algorithm-optimized social feeds. Users take a photo, send it to a group they've joined or created, and the app assembles group photos into a machine-learning-generated collage ("wall") rather than a chronological or algorithmic feed. The product has no likes and no public feed by design, and photos can be delivered directly to friends' lock screens. TechCrunch reports 2.2 million monthly active users and 800,000 daily active users as of February 2025, with 40% seven-day retention, an 18-year-old average user age, and 30x user-base growth in the prior six months — genuinely exceptional early-stage consumer engagement metrics.

### Thesis: why invest

Yope raised a $4.65m seed round at a $50m valuation, led by Goodwater Capital with Inovo VC and Redseed participating, alongside a notable angel group (Jean de La Rochebrochard, and Reface co-founder/a16z scout Dima Shvets, among others), per TechCrunch's February 2025 report. Goodwater — a repeat, credible consumer-social investor also behind Beli and Posh in this same batch — specifically framed Yope as "a prime example of an important new social behavior," a genuine third-party endorsement from a specialist investor.

The retention and growth numbers are the strongest raw engagement metrics of any consumer-social company in this batch: 40% D7 retention and 30x six-month growth are difficult to manufacture and suggest real product-market fit with Gen Z users specifically. The company has disclosed zero monetization, however — no subscription tier, no ads, no brand product of any kind is described anywhere in HCP's research. This is the earliest-stage, least-monetized company in the batch by a wide margin, which is why the recommendation is Watch despite the standout engagement data.

**What must be true:** engagement must persist as the app scales past its earliest, most enthusiastic cohort; a monetization product must be found that does not compromise the "no algorithm, no performance" positioning that differentiates Yope from Instagram/BeReal; and growth must extend beyond the current concentrated 18-year-old-average demographic.

**Next-round milestones:** any disclosed monetization test or product, DAU/MAU sustained or growing past the reported February 2025 levels, retention data beyond D7 (D30, D90), and international/demographic expansion evidence.

### Founder bet

Ismailau and Rudkouski's path to Yope reportedly involved multiple prior product pivots over several years before finding this specific format — a pattern that can reflect either genuine founder-market learning or a team still searching for durable fit. The current metrics suggest the former, but HCP should confirm the founders' specific role in past pivots and their operating discipline directly.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Global Gen Z close-friend photo-sharing willing-to-pay population | 70m | $12 | $840m | HCP assumption: entirely hypothetical, no monetization disclosed by the company |
| **TAM** | | | **$840m** | Annual revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **5.4% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$45m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **1** | **3** | **8** | **16** | **26** | **36** | **45** |

Yope has disclosed no revenue or monetization plan publicly. This table is an HCP construction built to stress-test the check, not a company projection.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Yope** | Private-group, feed-less photo sharing | X photo sharing, group walls; No evidence monetization | Mobile app | 40% D7 retention and 30x six-month growth (strongest raw engagement in this batch) | Free; no monetization disclosed | $4.65m seed at $50m valuation; Goodwater Capital, Inovo VC, Redseed |
| BeReal | Once-daily authentic photo-sharing prompt | X photo sharing; Partial private-group focus | Mobile app | Early "anti-Instagram" brand recognition | Freemium (limited monetization disclosed) | Private (acquired by Voodoo); capital data not comparable |
| Instagram (Close Friends) | General social feed with a private-sharing feature | Partial private sharing; X primary product is public feed | Native app | Massive existing user base and ad infrastructure | Ad-supported | Meta product |
| Locket | Widget-based photo sharing with close friends | X widget-based sharing; Partial group (mostly 1:1) focus | Mobile app widget | Early widget-based virality | Freemium | Private; capital data undisclosed here |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Reddit](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/rddt/statistics/) | 12.99x | High-growth, highly engaged consumer-social comp |
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | High-engagement consumer-discovery comp |
| [Snap](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/snap/statistics/) | 1.48x | Closest demographic comp (younger-skewing photo/social) |
| [Bumble](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/bmbl/statistics/) | 0.85x | Social-matching consumer comp |
| **Median** | **2.215x** | HCP uses 1.0x, well below median given total absence of monetization evidence |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $50m, disclosed (TechCrunch, February 2025 seed round) |
| Initial ownership | 3.00% ($1.5m / $50m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 1.95% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $45m / 1.0x |
| Exit enterprise value | $45m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $0.8775m / **0.585x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.351x / 1.755x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($27m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (already at the 1.0x floor, so unchanged) yields $27m EV, $0.5265m proceeds, 0.351x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($67.5m) at 2.0x yields $135m EV, $2.6325m proceeds, 1.755x MOIC.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Zero monetization evidence:** the standout engagement metrics have not been tested against a single dollar of revenue. This is the central diligence gap.
- **Demographic concentration and durability:** an 18-year-old average user age is a strong early signal but also a cohort known for rapid platform-switching. Confirm whether engagement holds as the earliest cohort ages or as growth broadens.
- **Founder pivot history:** multiple prior products before Yope raises a question of whether this is the durable format or the latest iteration. Confirm directly with founders.
- **Why watch rather than pass:** Goodwater's direct, specific investment thesis ("an important new social behavior") from a repeat consumer-social investor, combined with genuinely rare retention numbers, makes this worth tracking closely for the first monetization signal rather than dismissing outright.

## 98. Posh

**Stage:** Series B *(exception explained — see note at top of file)*
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://posh.vip/) | [Series A report](https://www.forbes.com/sites/dariashunina/2024/07/23/posh-raises-22m-to-power-your-social-life/) | [Series B report](https://fortune.com/2026/03/19/exclusive-posh-lands-37m-series-b-what-are-we-doing-tonight-problem/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Avante Price | Co-founder and CEO | Forbes profiles Price, who grew up DJing in Chicago and dropped out of NYU to launch Posh with Taylor-Lemire. |
| Eli Taylor-Lemire | Co-founder and CPO | Forbes identifies Taylor-Lemire, who previously ran a freelance photo/video agency producing content for major artists, as co-founder and product lead; also an NYU dropout. |

### Product description

Posh is a mobile-first event discovery and ticketing platform, described in press coverage as "the TikTok of events" for its vertical-scroll discovery feed. Rather than focusing on major venues or ticketed arena shows, Posh emphasizes grassroots and community events — club nights, run clubs, pop-up dinners, warehouse parties, fashion shows, and festivals — giving independent organizers discovery, ticketing, checkout, and analytics tools in one platform. Founded in 2019, the company has grown to more than 2 million registered users and reports roughly $40m in cumulative revenue and $350m in gross ticket volume since inception, with a case study organizer ("Not a Run Club") citing 122 events and 2,889 attendees through the platform.

### Thesis: why invest

Posh's financing history is unusually well documented for this batch: a $5m seed in 2023, a $22m Series A in July 2024 led by Goodwater Capital (with FirstMark, Companyon Ventures, Epic Ventures, and Day One Ventures), and — critically for this memo's pricing — a $37m Series B in March 2026 led by FirstMark Capital at a disclosed $253m valuation, with Causeway Ventures, Goodwater Capital, Companyon Ventures, and Epic Ventures also participating, per Fortune's exclusive report (corroborated by TheSaaSNews, Finsmes, and a funding-tracking account's post of the round's term-sheet-style summary). This is one of only two companies in this batch with a fully disclosed, multi-outlet-corroborated current valuation.

That same disclosed valuation is the problem for this memo. At $253m post-money, a $1.5m check buys roughly 0.59% before dilution, and even a healthy 2032 revenue outcome ($150m, built bottom-up from a plausible GMV and take-rate path) at a market-appropriate ticketing multiple does not clear a 1.0x base MOIC once that ownership is diluted further to exit. Posh looks like a genuinely good business — real users, real GMV, credible investors across three rounds — but it is priced, at this entry point and check size, past the return threshold this program targets.

**What must be true:** either a materially lower effective entry price (a secondary purchase at a discount, or participation in a future down-round or flat extension) or a revenue outcome well above HCP's base case (driven by AI-organizer tooling meaningfully lifting GMV per organizer, per the company's own stated Series B thesis) would be required to clear an attractive MOIC at this check size — absent one of those, this stays a Pass.

**Next-round milestones:** disclosed current-run-rate revenue (not just cumulative-since-inception figures), evidence that AI-organizer tools are lifting GMV per active organizer, and any secondary or structured entry opportunity below the primary $253m mark — these are re-underwriting triggers, not near-term expectations.

### Founder bet

Price and Taylor-Lemire's non-traditional founder paths (DJ and photo/video agency backgrounds, both NYU dropouts) map directly onto the product's grassroots-events focus, and three successive institutional rounds from credible investors (Goodwater across two rounds, FirstMark leading the Series B) suggest sustained investor conviction in the team's execution. The founder bet is not the issue with this file — the entry price is.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | GMV | Take rate | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Grassroots/community event GMV addressable in the US | $15.0bn | 8% blended take | $1.20bn | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$1.20bn** | Annual net-revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **12.5% of TAM revenue** | Reflects Posh's reported category-leading position in curated small-event discovery |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$150m** | HCP base case |

|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| GMV | 250 | 400 | 600 | 850 | 1,150 | 1,500 | 1,900 |
| Blended take rate | 6% | 6.5% | 7% | 7.5% | 8% | 8% | 8% |
| **Revenue** | **15** | **26** | **42** | **64** | **92** | **120** | **150** |

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Posh** | Grassroots/community event discovery and ticketing | X discovery, ticketing, checkout, organizer analytics | Mobile app, vertical-feed discovery | Community/grassroots-event focus and organizer relationships | Ticketing/processing fees, exact rate undisclosed | $37m Series B at $253m valuation; $64m total across 3 rounds; FirstMark, Goodwater, Causeway, Companyon, Epic |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Shopify](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/shop/statistics/) | 12.49x | Broad commerce-platform comp (less directly relevant) |
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | Consumer-discovery comp |
| [Eventbrite](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/eb/statistics/) | 0.77x | Closest business-model comp (event ticketing) |
| [Vivid Seats](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/seat/statistics/) | 0.63x | Ticketing-marketplace comp |
| **Median** | **1.86x** | HCP uses 1.5x, reflecting thin ticketing-industry margins tempered by some credit for the curated-discovery layer |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $253m, disclosed (Series B, March 2026) |
| Initial ownership | 0.593% ($1.5m / $253m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 0.385% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $150m / 1.5x |
| Exit enterprise value | $225m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $0.867m / **0.578x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.231x / 1.445x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($90m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (1.5x − 1 turn = 0.5x, floored to 1.0x) yields $90m EV, $0.3465m proceeds, 0.231x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($225m) at 2.5x yields $562.5m EV, $2.168m proceeds, 1.445x MOIC — even the upside case falls short of a strong return at this entry price.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Entry price:** the core issue. At a $253m post-money, this program's check size cannot buy enough ownership to clear an attractive MOIC under any reasonable revenue scenario modeled here. HCP should not pursue at this price.
- **Ticketing-margin structure:** the comp set (Eventbrite, Vivid Seats) trades below 1.0x EV/revenue, reflecting a structurally thin-margin category regardless of Posh's execution quality.
- **Revenue disclosure gap:** the $40m "cumulative revenue since inception" figure does not establish a current run rate; HCP's $150m 2032 figure could be too high or too low without better data.
- **Why this is a Pass, not a Watch:** unlike Yope or 222, where the gap is evidence, Posh's problem is structural (price and category economics) and would not be resolved by more information at the current terms — only a materially different entry price would change the conclusion.

## 99. Pie

**Stage:** Series A
**Proposed HCP check:** $1.5m
**Recommendation:** Pass
**Links:** [Company](https://getpie.app/) | [Series A report](https://techcrunch.com/2025/03/04/andy-dunns-new-app-pie-uses-ai-to-help-you-make-friends/) | [Additional coverage](https://techcrunch.com/2024/11/19/irl-social-app-pie-is-coming-to-sf-to-make-you-less-lonely/)

### Founders and company

| Founder | Role | Relevant evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Andy Dunn | Co-founder and CEO | TechCrunch identifies Dunn, who co-founded menswear brand Bonobos and led it as CEO through its 2017 acquisition by Walmart, as Pie's founder. |
| Samir Mahafzah | Co-founder | TechCrunch reports Mahafzah and Stubbs built a tool called Sparked Connections that was acqui-hired into Pie; confirm current role in diligence. |
| Sam Stubbs | Co-founder | Co-built Sparked Connections alongside Mahafzah prior to joining Pie. |

### Product description

Pie is an app that uses an AI-powered personality quiz to assemble small groups (around six people) of compatible strangers for in-person events, then pays local organizers to actually run those events — a deliberate design choice to guarantee events happen rather than relying on unpaid volunteer hosts or open RSVPs that can fall apart. As of the March 2025 TechCrunch report, Pie had more than 130,000 monthly active users but operated in only two cities, San Francisco and Chicago. Note on sourcing: the roster hint "trypie.com" for this company actually resolves to an unrelated business, Pie Insurance (a small-business insurance provider); the correct official site for the friendship app is getpie.app, confirmed by TechCrunch's March 2025 coverage.

### Thesis: why invest

Pie raised an $11.5m Series A led by Kirsten Green of Forerunner Ventures, with Origin Ventures, Renegade Partners, and Twitter co-founder Ev Williams among the participants, per Pulse2's reporting; total disclosed funding is $24m. Andy Dunn's Bonobos pedigree is a genuine positive signal — he has built and scaled a consumer brand to a nine-figure acquisition before — and the paid-organizer model is a thoughtful structural choice that should improve event reliability relative to open-RSVP competitors.

The concern is unit economics, not product quality. Pie pays organizers to host events, which is a real cash cost embedded in the core product loop, and the company has disclosed no revenue, pricing, or membership model to offset that cost. Combined with a footprint still limited to two cities after roughly a year and a half of operation (per the November 2024 and March 2025 TechCrunch pieces), the growth rate looks materially slower than Timeleft's expansion to 200+ cities over a comparable period, and slower than 222's move from one city to two. At any plausible current valuation, HCP's bottom-up model — built conservatively given the negative-cost-structure starting point — does not clear a positive base-case MOIC.

**What must be true:** Pie must disclose a monetization plan that more than offsets the cost of paying organizers; the two-city footprint must expand meaningfully, demonstrating the model travels; and MAU growth must translate into event-attendance frequency data, not just app opens — absent that, this stays a Pass.

**Next-round milestones:** expansion to at least 5 cities, a disclosed monetization test, evidence that paid-organizer unit economics improve with scale (lower subsidy per event as density increases), and updated MAU/attendance figures beyond the March 2025 disclosure — these are re-underwriting triggers, not near-term expectations.

### Founder bet

Dunn's track record (Bonobos, sold to Walmart for a reported nine-figure sum) is real and relevant — he has proven he can build a consumer brand people love and eventually monetize it. The acqui-hire of Mahafzah and Stubbs's Sparked Connections suggests a deliberate, product-informed team-building approach rather than a solo-founder vanity project. HCP's Pass recommendation reflects the current evidence and stage, not doubt about the team; this is a file to revisit if the city footprint and monetization picture change materially.

### Market, TAM, and revenue build

| Bottom-up step | Units | Annual value | Result | Basis |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Urban young professionals in Pie-reachable US metros | 12m | $40 | $480m | HCP assumption |
| Corporate/employer wellness partnerships | — | — | $40m | HCP assumption |
| **TAM** | | | **$520m** | Annual revenue pool |
| HCP penetration | | | **6.7% of TAM revenue** | HCP base case, discounted for the current 2-city footprint and cost structure |
| **2032 revenue opportunity** | | | **$35m** | HCP base case |

| Revenue driver, $m | 2026E | 2027E | 2028E | 2029E | 2030E | 2031E | 2032E |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| **Revenue** | **1** | **3** | **7** | **13** | **20** | **28** | **35** |

Pie has disclosed no revenue publicly, and its current model (paying organizers) is a net cost rather than a revenue source. This table is a conservative HCP construction, not a company projection.

### Competitive landscape

| Company | Category / user | Workflow | Delivery | Moat | Pricing | Capital status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Pie** | AI-matched small-group friendship events | X AI matching; X paid-organizer event hosting | Mobile app, 2-city footprint | AI personality quiz plus guaranteed event execution via paid organizers | Undisclosed; current model is a net cost, not confirmed revenue | $11.5m Series A; $24m total; valuation undisclosed; Forerunner Ventures, Origin Ventures, Renegade Partners |
| Timeleft | Scheduled stranger-dinner matching | X matching, weekly recurring dinners; 200+-city footprint | Mobile app | Disclosed real revenue and far larger footprint | Per-event fee | See this batch's Timeleft memo |
| 222 | AI-matched curated experiences | X matching and event booking; 2-city footprint | Mobile app | AI personality-assessment matching, strong investor syndicate | Undisclosed | See this batch's 222 memo |
| Meetup | Interest-group event listings | Partial matching; X organizer-run events without algorithmic curation | Web/app | Long-standing installed base | Organizer subscription | Private; capital data undisclosed here |

### Public comps and exit model

| Public comp | EV/LTM revenue | Relevance |
|---|---:|---|
| [Reddit](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/rddt/statistics/) | 12.99x | High-growth consumer-social comp |
| [Pinterest](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/pins/statistics/) | 2.95x | Consumer-discovery comp |
| [Snap](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/snap/statistics/) | 1.48x | Younger-skewing consumer-social comp |
| [Bumble](https://stockanalysis.com/stocks/bmbl/statistics/) | 0.85x | Social-matching consumer comp |
| **Median** | **2.215x** | HCP uses 1.0x, well below median given zero disclosed revenue and a cost-negative core loop |

| Return path | Base |
|---|---:|
| Entry post-money | $55m, HCP assumption |
| Initial ownership | 2.727% ($1.5m / $55m) |
| Cumulative future dilution | 35%, HCP assumption |
| Exit ownership | 1.7727% |
| 2032 revenue / exit multiple | $35m / 1.0x |
| Exit enterprise value | $35m |
| HCP proceeds / MOIC | $0.620m / **0.414x** |
| Downside / upside MOIC | 0.248x / 1.241x |

Downside detail: 60% of base revenue ($21m) at a floored 1.0x multiple (already at the 1.0x floor, so unchanged) yields $21m EV, $0.372m proceeds, 0.248x MOIC. Upside: 150% of base revenue ($52.5m) at 2.0x yields $105m EV, $1.861m proceeds, 1.241x MOIC — even the upside case falls short of an attractive return.

### Principal risks and why invest anyway

- **Negative-cost core loop:** paying organizers to run events is a real, ongoing cash cost with no disclosed offsetting revenue. This is the central problem with the file as it stands today.
- **Slow geographic expansion:** two cities after roughly 18 months, versus much faster footprint growth at Timeleft and even 222. Confirm whether this reflects deliberate quality-first strategy or a harder-to-scale operating model.
- **No disclosed monetization:** unlike Timeleft, there is no revenue evidence at all to anchor a base case.
- **Why this is a Pass, not a Watch:** the combination of a real, ongoing cost (paid organizers) with zero offsetting revenue evidence and slower-than-peer geographic expansion makes this the weakest risk/reward file in the batch; HCP would need to see the cost structure and city count change materially before re-engaging, which is a higher bar than the "wait for one data point" framing used for the batch's Watch recommendations.
